Conditions for the Validity of Iqalah
Lists and explains seven conditions for a valid iqalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions for a valid iqalah and apply them to determine whether a given rescission is valid.

Core Idea
Iqalah requires mutual consent, existing goods, and session unity — without these it is void.

In this lesson, we examine the conditions that make an iqalah (rescission of a sale) legally effective. The Hanafi school lists seven requirements, each with a specific legal rationale. Understanding these conditions will enable you to assess the validity of an iqalah in various scenarios, including cases involving heirs, authorized persons, and executors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its purpose
Recognize that iqalah is the mutual rescission of a sale, returning each party to their original state. It is not a new sale but a dissolution.
This is a faskh (rescission), not a bay' (sale) in the Hanafi view.
2
Examine the first condition: consent
Both parties must consent because iqalah lifts a binding contract. However, for non-binding contracts (e.g., khiyar), the option-holder can cancel without the other's consent but must inform them.
Consent is not required when the contract itself is not binding.
3
Understand the subject matter condition
The sold item must still exist. If it perishes, iqalah is impossible because there is nothing to return.
This is similar to the condition for returning an item in a defective sale.
4
Analyze special conditions: sarf and increase
For currency exchange (sarf), both countervalues must be delivered in the session. For other sales, if the item has increased in a way that prevents rescission (e.g., buyer added construction), iqalah is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn differ.
The disagreement is noted; the text takes Abu Hanifa's view as the basis.
5
Cover the remaining conditions
These include: unity of session (offer and acceptance in one sitting), continued existence of the parties (heirs/executors can act), and restrictions for authorized persons and executors regarding gift of price and excessive value.
The later conditions address specific situations to prevent abuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما شرائط صحتها فمنها رضا المتعاقدين لأن الكلام في رفع عقد لازم، وأما رفع ما ليس بلازم فلمن له الخيار بعلم صاحبه لا برضاه. ومنها بقاء المحل لما سيأتي أن المبيع إذا هلك لم تصح الإقالة، ومنها قبض بدلي الصرف في إقالة الصرف، أما على قول أبي يوسف فظاهر لأنها بيع، وأما على أصلهما فلأنها بيع في حق ثالث وهو حق الشرع ومنها أن يكون المبيع قابلاً للفسخ بخيار من الخيارات فلو ازداد زيادة تمنع الفسخ لم تصح الإقالة خلافاً لهما. ولا يشترط لصحتها بقاء المتعاقدين فتصح إقالة الوارث والوصي ولا تصح إقالة الموصى له كما في القنية. ومنها اتحاد المجلس وعليه يتفرع ما في القنية : جاء الدلال بالثمن إلى البائع بعدما باعه بالأمر المطلق فقال البائع لا أدفعه بهذا الثمن فأخبر به المشتري فقال أنا لا أزيده أيضاً لا ينفسخ لأنه ليس من ألفاظ الفسخ لأن اتحاد المجلس في الإيجاب والقبول شرط في الإقالة ولم يوجد اهـ. ومنها أن لا يهب البائع الثمن للمشتري قبل قبضه في شراء المأذون، فلو وهبه لم تصح الإقالة بعدها كما في خزانة المفتين، ومنها أن لا يكون البيع بالكثير من القيمة في بيع الوصي فإن كان لم تصح إقالته كما فيها أيضاً .
As for the conditions of its validity: among them are the consent of the two contracting parties, because the discussion is about lifting a binding contract. As for lifting what is not binding, it is for the one who has the option, with the knowledge of his companion, not with his consent. Among them is the continued existence of the subject matter, as will come that if the sold item perishes, iqalah is not valid. Among them is the delivery of the countervalues in the iqalah of currency exchange (sarf). According to Abu Yusuf, it is apparent because it is a sale; and according to their principle, because it is a sale with respect to a third party, which is the right of the Law. Among them is that the sold item must be capable of being rescinded by a type of option; if an increase occurs that prevents rescission, iqalah is not valid, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The continued existence of the contracting parties is not a condition; thus iqalah of the heir and executor is valid, and iqalah of the legatee is not valid, as in al-Qunyah. Among them is the unity of the session, and based on this is what is in al-Qunyah: the broker came with the price to the seller after he had sold by absolute order, and the seller said, 'I will not pay it at this price.' The buyer was informed and said, 'I will not increase it either.' It is not rescinded because it is not from the words of rescission, because unity of session in offer and acceptance is a condition in iqalah, and it was not found. End quote. Among them is that the seller should not gift the price to the buyer before taking possession in the purchase of an authorized person, for if he gifts it, iqalah after it is not valid, as in Khizanat al-Muftiyin. Among them is that the sale should not be for an excessive value in the sale of an executor; if it is, his iqalah is not valid, as also therein.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage lists the conditions for a valid iqalah. The first condition is the consent of both parties since iqalah involves lifting a binding contract. However, if the contract is non-binding (e.g., the buyer has an option), the one with the option can cancel without the other's consent, but must inform them. Second, the subject matter (the sold item) must still exist; if it perishes, iqalah is impossible. Third, in the case of currency exchange (sarf), both countervalues must be delivered in the session; this is because iqalah is considered a sale with respect to third parties. Fourth, the sold item must be capable of rescission; if it has increased in a way that prevents rescission (e.g., the buyer added construction), iqalah is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ. Fifth, the contracting parties themselves need not survive; their heirs or executors can perform iqalah. Sixth, the session must be continuous; if the offer and acceptance are separated by a break, iqalah is not valid. Seventh, in certain special cases (like purchase by an authorized person or sale by executor), gifting the price or excessive value prevents iqalah. These conditions ensure that iqalah is a valid rescission and not abused.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqalah): The mutual rescission of a sale, returning each party to their original state.
اتحاد المجلس (ittihad al-majlis): The condition that offer and acceptance occur in the same session without significant interruption.
رضا المتعاقدين (rida al-muta'aqidayn): Consent of the two contracting parties.
بدلي الصرف (badalay al-sarf): The two countervalues in a currency exchange transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of iqalah?
A) Consent of both parties
B) Existence of the sold item
C) The seller must be the original owner
D) Unity of session

Key Takeaway
A valid iqalah requires mutual consent, an existing subject matter, session unity, and fulfillment of special conditions for sarf, increases, and specific parties.

The Legal Nature of Iqalah: Rescission or Sale?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on iqalah's nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of iqalah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over its legal nature (faskh vs bay') across different scenarios.

Core Idea
Iqalah is rescission (faskh) by default but may be a sale when price or subject changes.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes the ruling on iqalah (mutual cancellation of a sale) and then dives into a nuanced intra-Hanafi debate: is iqalah a rescission of the original contract (faskh) or a new sale (bay')? The answer depends on factors like timing (before or after possession), type of property, and whether the price changes. Understanding this dispute clarifies the legal consequences for delivery, options, and third-party rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on iqalah
State that iqalah is recommended (sunnah) based on the hadith, and note that it becomes wajib if the original contract is makruh tahrimi.
The hadith is ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut.
2
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute on legal nature
List the positions: Abu Hanifa: faskh always; Abu Yusuf: sale always; Muhammad: faskh if price same/less, sale if more/different; Zufar: faskh always.
The text distinguishes before/after possession and movable/real estate.
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: if iqalah is a sale, delivery of countervalues and options of sight apply; if faskh, the contract is simply undone.
This affects the rights of third parties.
4
Note the exception for third parties
All imams agree that iqalah is a sale with respect to third parties, even Abu Hanifa.
This ensures protection of third-party rights.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Given a buyer regrets after possession and seller accepts iqalah with a higher price, determine the nature according to each imam and the required actions.
According to Muhammad, it is a sale because price increased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما صفتها فهي مندوب إليها للحديث من أقال نادماً . بيعته يوم القيام (۱) وقدمنا أنها تكون واجبة إذا كان عقداً مكروهاً، وينبغي أن تكون واجبة إذا كان (فيه الخ) قال في الجوهرة: إن كانت قبل القبض فهي فسخ إجماعاً وإن كانت بعد القبض فهي فسخ عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : هي .بيع. وقال محمد: إن كانت بالثمن الأول أو بأقل فهي فسخ، وإن كانت بأكثر أو بجنس آخر فهي بيع، ولا خلاف بينهم أنها بيع في حق الغير سواء كانت قبل القبض أو بعده وقال :زفر هي فسخ في حقهما وحق الغير اهـ. وفي العناية : والإقالة في المنقول قبل القبض فسخ بالاتفاق لامتناع البيع، وأما في غيره كالعقار فإنه فسخ عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وأما عند أبي يوسف فبيع الجواز البيع في العقار قبل القبض عنده اهـ. فظهر أن قول الجوهرة «إن كانت قبل القبض فهي فسخ إجماعاً» محمول على المنقول وقولها «ولا خلاف بينهم الخ» يخالفه قول الزيلعي وإن كانت قبل القبض فهي فسخ في حق الكل في غير العقار لتعذر جعلها بيعاً» (۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب البيوع باب ٥٢ ابن ماجه في كتاب التجارات باب ٢٦. أحمد في مسنده (٢٥٢/٢) بلفظ (من أقال مسلماً أقاله الله عثرته».
As for its description, it is recommended due to the hadith: 'Whoever grants a release to a regretful person, Allah will grant him release on the Day of Resurrection.' And we have presented that it becomes wajib if the contract is makruh tahrimi, and it should be wajib if... (then the rest). (There is a detailed discussion) al-Jawharah said: If it is before possession, it is faskh by consensus. If it is after possession, it is faskh according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: it is a sale. Muhammad said: if it is with the first price or less, it is faskh; if with more or a different genus, it is a sale. And there is no difference among them that it is a sale with respect to a third party, whether before or after possession. Zufar said: it is faskh in the rights of both and the right of a third party. End quote. In al-'Inayah: iqalah of movables before possession is faskh by agreement due to impossibility of sale. As for other than that, like real estate, it is faskh according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a permissible sale in real estate before possession? End quote. So it appears that the statement of al-Jawharah 'If before possession, it is faskh by consensus' is restricted to movables, and her statement 'there is no difference among them' contradicts al-Zayla'i: 'if before possession, it is faskh for all in other than real estate because it is impossible to make it a sale.' (1) Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Buyu', Bab 52; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Tijarat, Bab 26; Ahmad in his Musnad (2/252) with the wording: 'Whoever grants a release to a Muslim, Allah will grant him release from his stumble.'
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage first establishes the basic ruling on iqalah: it is recommended (sunnah), supported by a hadith that promises divine reward for those who accept a release from a regretful buyer. However, it may become wajib if the original sale was makruh tahrimi (disliked to the point of prohibition), as cancelling it removes sin. The second part of the passage dives into the legal nature of iqalah: is it a rescission (faskh) or a new sale (bay')? There is a well-known intra-Hanafi debate. According to al-Jawharah, if iqalah occurs before the buyer takes possession, it is unanimously considered a rescission (faskh). After possession, Abu Hanifa still considers it faskh, Abu Yusuf considers it a new sale, and Muhammad distinguishes: if the price is the original or less, it is faskh; if more or a different type, it is a sale. All agree it is a sale with respect to third parties. Later texts like al-'Inayah refine this: the consensus on faskh before possession applies only to movable goods; for real estate, there is disagreement even before possession. This analysis affects rules like the need for delivery of countervalues in currency exchange. The relied-upon position is that iqalah is fundamentally a rescission, but in some contexts it is treated as a sale.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; undoing the contract as if it never existed.
بيع (bay'): A new sale contract; iqalah is considered a sale when the price differs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling of iqalah when the original sale is makruh tahrimi?
A) Sunnah (recommended)
B) Wajib (obligatory)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is recommended but may become wajib; its legal nature (faskh or bay') varies among Hanafi imams depending on timing and price.

Pillars and Conditions of Iqalah (Rescission of Sale)
Defines iqalah and lists pillars and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rukn of iqalah and list its conditions of validity, distinguishing between the views of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on verbal forms.

Core Idea
Iqalah is a rescission of sale; its pillar is offer and acceptance, and it has seven key conditions.

The passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq defines iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) and details its structural elements. You will learn that the rukn is offer and acceptance, which can be expressed in various verbal forms or even by action. The conditions for validity include mutual consent, existence of the subject matter, unity of session, and special rules for currency exchange, executors, and minors. Understanding these conditions is essential to correctly execute or judge an iqalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rukn (pillar) of iqalah
The passage states that the rukn is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul) indicating rescission. Note that different imams differ on whether both must be in past tense or one can be future.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow one future and one past; Imam Muhammad requires both past.
2
List the valid expressions for iqalah
Besides standard phrases like 'iqilni' and 'aqaltuka', other words like 'fāsakhtuka', 'taraktu', etc., are valid. Even actions like cutting a garment can constitute acceptance.
Iqalah can also be concluded by mutual giving (ta'ati) without words.
3
Enumerate the conditions of validity (shurut al-sihhah)
The passage lists several conditions: mutual consent, existence of the mahal, hand-to-hand payment in sarf, the sold item being subject to rescission, unity of session, no gifting of price to a minor buyer, and executor's sale not being grossly undervalued.
Some conditions have exceptions (e.g., non-binding contracts require only knowledge, not consent).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the verbal form
Compare Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf's view (one future permissible) with Imam Muhammad's (both past). Understand the analogy to nikah vs. sale.
This is a minor ikhtilaf within the school; the practical impact is on which expressions are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رفع النكاح. وأما ركنها فالإيجاب والقبول الدالان عليها بلفظين ماضيين أو أحدهما مستقبلاً والآخر ماضياً كاقلني فقال أقلتك عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف كالنكاح. وقال محمد : لا تنعقد إلا بماضيين كالبيع ؛ كذا في البدائع. وقد يكون القبول بالفعل كما لو قطعه قميصاً في فور قول المشتري أقلتك، وتنعقد بفاسختك وتركت وتاركتك ودفعت وتنعقد بالتعاطي كالبيع كما في الخانية والخلاصة. وفي البزازية ينعقد به كالبيع من أحد الجانبين وهو الصحيح. وأما شرائط صحتها فمنها رضا المتعاقدين لأن الكلام في رفع عقد لازم، وأما رفع ما ليس بلازم فلمن له الخيار بعلم صاحبه لا برضاه. ومنها بقاء المحل لما سيأتي أن المبيع إذا هلك لم تصح الإقالة، ومنها قبض بدلي الصرف في إقالة الصرف، أما على قول أبي يوسف فظاهر لأنها بيع، وأما على أصلهما فلأنها بيع في حق ثالث وهو حق الشرع ومنها أن يكون المبيع قابلاً للفسخ بخيار من الخيارات فلو ازداد زيادة تمنع الفسخ لم تصح الإقالة خلافاً لهما. ولا يشترط لصحتها بقاء المتعاقدين فتصح إقالة الوارث والوصي ولا تصح إقالة الموصى له كما في القنية. ومنها اتحاد المجلس وعليه يتفرع ما في القنية : جاء الدلال بالثمن إلى البائع بعدما باعه بالأمر المطلق فقال البائع لا أدفعه بهذا الثمن فأخبر به المشتري فقال أنا لا أزيده أيضاً لا ينفسخ لأنه ليس من ألفاظ الفسخ لأن اتحاد المجلس في الإيجاب والقبول شرط في الإقالة ولم يوجد اهـ. ومنها أن لا يهب البائع الثمن للمشتري قبل قبضه في شراء المأذون، فلو وهبه لم تصح الإقالة بعدها كما في خزانة المفتين، ومنها أن لا يكون البيع بالكثير من القيمة في بيع الوصي فإن كان لم تصح إقالته كما فيها أيضاً
Rescission of the contract. As for its pillar, it is offer and acceptance that indicate it, either with two past-tense verbs or one future and the other past, like 'iqilni' and the other says 'aqaltuka' according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, similar to marriage. Muhammad said: It is only concluded with two past-tense verbs like a sale; thus in al-Bada'i. Acceptance may be by action, such as him cutting a shirt immediately upon the buyer saying 'aqaltuka'. It is concluded with 'fāsakhtuka', 'taraktu', 'tāraktuka', and 'dafa'tu', and it is concluded by mutual giving (ta'ati) like a sale as in al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa. In al-Bazzaziyya, it is concluded by mutual giving from one side, and that is correct. As for the conditions of its validity: among them is the consent of the two contracting parties because the discussion is about revoking a binding contract. As for revoking a non-binding contract, then the one with the option may do so with the knowledge of the other, not with his consent. Among them is the continued existence of the object (mahal) because the sold item if destroyed, the iqalah is not valid. Among them is taking possession of the two countervalues in iqalah of currency exchange; as for Abu Yusuf's opinion, it is apparent because it is a sale; and as for their principle, it is a sale with regard to a third party, which is the right of the law. Among them is that the sold item must be subject to rescission by one of the options; if it has increased in a way that prevents rescission, iqalah is not valid, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The continued existence of the contracting parties is not a condition; thus iqalah of the heir and executor is valid, and iqalah of the legatee is not valid, as in al-Qunyah. Among them is unity of the session (ittihad al-majlis); and upon it branches what is in al-Qunyah: The broker brought the price to the seller after he sold it by absolute command, and the seller said 'I will not pay this price,' so the buyer was informed and said 'I also will not increase it'; it does not dissolve because it is not from the words of rescission, because unity of session in offer and acceptance is a condition in iqalah and it was not found. End. Among them is that the seller should not gift the price to the buyer before taking possession in the purchase of a minor (ma'dhun); if he gifts it, iqalah is not valid afterwards, as in Khizanat al-Muftiyin. Among them is that the sale should not be at a much higher price in the sale of an executor; if it was, his iqalah is not valid, as also mentioned there.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq defines iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) and explains its pillars and conditions. The author begins by stating that the rukn (pillar) of iqalah is offer and acceptance. The offer and acceptance can be expressed by two past-tense verbs, or one future and one past tense, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. However, Imam Muhammad requires both to be past tense, similar to a sale contract. The author then notes that acceptance can be by action (e.g., cutting a garment) immediately after the offer, which is valid. Other valid expressions include ‘fāsakhtuka’ (I revoke), ‘taraktu’ (I left), ‘tāraktuka’ (I forsook you), and ‘dafa'tu’ (I paid). Iqalah can also be concluded by mutual giving (ta'ati) without verbal expression, as is the case with sales.
Next, the conditions of validity (shurut al-sihhah) are listed:
1. Mutual consent of the parties, since iqalah revokes a binding contract. For revoking a non-binding contract (e.g., one with an option), only the knowledge of the other party is needed, not consent.
2. The subject matter (al-mahal) must still exist; if the sold item is destroyed, iqalah is invalid.
3. In iqalah of currency exchange (sarf), the two countervalues must be physically exchanged in the session, as per the requirement of hand-to-hand transaction. This is because iqalah is considered a sale in effect.
4. The sold item must be capable of being rescinded by any type of option; if it has increased in value or quantity in a way that prevents rescission (like an increase that is non-separable), iqalah is invalid. This is the view of Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree.
5. The existence of the original parties is not required, so the heir or executor can perform iqalah, but the legatee cannot.
6. Unity of the session (ittihad al-majlis) is required, meaning that the offer and acceptance must occur in the same sitting. The author gives an example: if a broker brings the price but the seller refuses, and the buyer also refuses, the contract is not dissolved because the unity of session is missing.
7. In the case of a purchase by a minor (ma'dhun), the seller should not gift the price to the minor before taking possession, because then iqalah would be invalid.
8. In a sale by an executor, if the sale was at a grossly undervalued price (much more than value), the executor's iqalah is invalid.
These conditions ensure that iqalah is properly executed and does not harm the rights of parties.

Key Terms
الإقالة (al-iqālah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract by agreement of the parties
اتحاد المجلس (ittiḥād al-majlis): Unity of session; condition that offer and acceptance must occur in the same sitting
ركن (rukn): Pillar; an essential component without which the contract is invalid
شرط (shart): Condition; a requirement that must be fulfilled for validity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for the validity of iqalah according to the passage?
A) The presence of the original seller and buyer at the time of iqalah
B) The sold item must not have increased in a way that prevents rescission
C) The iqalah must be performed in a mosque
D) Both parties must use past-tense verbs

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is a valid mutual rescission of a sale, with its pillar being offer and acceptance, and it requires several conditions including consent, existence of the subject matter, unity of session, and special rules for currency exchange, minors, and executors.

The Ruling and Legal Nature of Iqalah
Ruling and legal nature of iqalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling of iqalah, identify the two cases where it becomes wajib, and explain the four Hanafi opinions on whether iqalah is a rescission (faskh) or a new sale (bay') and the practical consequences.

Core Idea
Iqalah is recommended but becomes wajib when the sale was makruh or the seller slightly deceived; its legal nature is rescission, but treated as a sale for third parties.

This lesson examines iqalah (rescission of a sale) from two angles: its descriptive ruling (whether it is mandub or wajib) and its legal nature (whether it is a rescission or a new sale). The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on the latter, with Abu Hanifa adopting a nuanced position that splits the effects between the parties and third parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects discussed
The passage first addresses the hukm taklifi (recommended/obligatory) using the hadith and conditions, then the hukm wad'i (legal nature) as faskh or bay'.
2
Extract the default ruling from the hadith
The hadith 'Whoever rescinds a sale with a regretful person, Allah will forgive his sins' indicates recommendation (mandub) because the promise of reward implies desirability, not obligation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is mandub, not fard.
3
Identify when iqalah becomes wajib
Iqalah becomes wajib in two situations: (1) when the original sale was makruh (disliked), and (2) when the seller deceived the buyer with slight ghabn (price discrepancy). If ghabn is gross (fahish), the buyer has the option to return the item, so iqalah is not obligatory.
Slight ghabn is defined later; gross ghabn gives the right of return, but the passage does not specify the threshold here.
4
Map the four Hanafi opinions on legal nature
Abu Hanifa: faskh for parties, new sale for third party. Abu Yusuf: sale for all. Muhammad: faskh for all. Zufar: faskh for all. Note that Muhammad and Zufar agree, but the dispute is between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
The text mentions these four opinions from al-Bada'i' and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
5
Determine the practical consequences
If iqalah is a sale (Abu Yusuf), pre-emption (shuf'a) applies, the price must be exactly the same, and creditors' rights are fully protected. If it is a rescission (Muhammad, Zufar), pre-emption does not apply and any adjustment to the price would invalidate it. Abu Hanifa's middle view treats it as rescission between parties (no pre-emption) but a sale for third parties to protect creditors.
The thamarah al-khilaf affects practical rulings in sale contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما صفتها فهي مندوب إليها للحديث من أقال نادماً . بيعته القيام (۱) وقدمنا أنها تكون واجبة إذا كان عقداً مكروهاً، وينبغي أن تكون واجبة إذا كان البائع غاراً للمشتري وكان الغبن يسيراً. وإنما قيدنا باليسير لأن الغبن الفاحش يوجب الرد إن غره البائع على الصحيح كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما حكمها فاختلف فيه على أقوال؛ فقال الإمام الأعظم : إنها فسخ في حق المتعاقدين بيع جديد في حق ثالث. وقال أبو يوسف : إنها بيع في حق الكل. وقال محمد فسخ في حق الكل. وقال زفر : هي فسخ في حق الكل ذكر قوله في البدائع والسراج الوهاج.
As for its quality (characteristic), it is recommended (mandub) due to the hadith: 'Whoever rescinds a sale with a regretful person, Allah will forgive his sins on the Day of Judgment.' And we have mentioned that it becomes obligatory if the contract is disliked (makruh), and it should be obligatory if the seller is deceiving the buyer and the deception is slight. We only restricted it to slight because gross deception necessitates return if the seller deceived, as will come with Allah's permission. As for its ruling (legal nature), there is a difference of opinion on statements: Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa) said: It is a rescission (faskh) regarding the two contracting parties and a new sale regarding a third party. Abu Yusuf said: It is a sale regarding all. Muhammad said: It is a rescission regarding all. Zufar said: It is a rescission regarding all. This is mentioned in al-Bada'i' and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses two aspects of iqalah: its descriptive ruling (hukm taklifi) and its legal nature (hukm wad'i).

First, the author states that the default ruling is that iqalah is recommended (mandub), based on the hadith: 'Whoever rescinds a sale with a regretful person, Allah will forgive his wrong steps on the Day of Resurrection.' This shows that performing iqalah is a praiseworthy act. However, it becomes obligatory (wajib) in two situations: (1) if the original sale itself was a disliked contract (makruh), then rescinding it is necessary to remove the sin; (2) if the seller deceived the buyer (gharar) and the deception (ghabn) is slight, then iqalah is obligatory to rectify the harm. But if the deception is gross (fahish), the buyer has the right to return the item due to the defect, so iqalah is not obligatory.

Second, the passage addresses the legal nature of iqalah: Is it a rescission (faskh) that reverts ownership to the original state, or is it a new sale (bay') that requires a fresh offer and acceptance? There are four opinions within the Hanafi school:
- Abu Hanifa (Imam al-A'zam): Iqalah is a rescission between the two parties but a new sale regarding a third party. This means that as far as the buyer and seller are concerned, the contract is annulled and ownership returns, but for third parties (like creditors), it is treated as a new sale to protect their rights.
- Abu Yusuf: Iqalah is a sale for all purposes, requiring all the rules of a sale transaction.
- Muhammad al-Shaybani: Iqalah is a rescission for all purposes.
- Zufar: Also says it is a rescission for all purposes.
The practical difference appears in issues like pre-emption (shuf'a), liability for defects, and the effect on creditors. The relied-upon position in the madhhab is that iqalah is a rescission, but for third parties it is treated as a sale according to Abu Hanifa, which is the dominant view.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment; returning the contract to its original state without a new transaction
الغبن (al-ghabn): Deception or discrepancy in price; slight ghabn is tolerated, gross ghabn gives right to return

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does iqalah become obligatory (wajib)?
A) Always, because it is recommended
B) When the seller is a close relative
C) When the original contract is disliked (makruh) or when the seller deceived the buyer with slight ghabn
D) Only when the buyer requests it

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is mandub but becomes wajib in cases of disliked contract or slight seller deception; its legal nature is predominantly rescission, with a sale-like treatment for third parties per Abu Hanifa.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Five Cases Where Iqalah is Invalid (The Exceptions)
Lists five exceptions where iqalah is invalid despite general authority to sell

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five exceptional cases where iqalah is invalid according to the Hanafi school and explain the general rule and the rationale for each exception.

Core Idea
Not every rescission is valid: five exceptions protect minors, orphans, waqf, and principals.

Iqalah is generally permissible for anyone with authority to sell. However, the Hanafi school identifies five specific situations where rescission is invalid, primarily to protect vulnerable parties. This lesson unpacks each exception and the reasoning behind it, including an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the agent for salam.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Whoever has authority to sell also has authority to perform iqalah. This is the baseline.
Applies to owners, agents for sale, etc.
2
Memorize the First Exception: Executor's Purchase
If an executor buys an undervalued asset from the orphan's debtor, then rescinds after collecting the debt, the iqalah is invalid.
Reason: the original sale was a settlement benefitting the orphan.
3
Memorize the Second Exception: Permitted Minor's Purchase
A permitted minor (ma'dhun) who buys an overvalued item cannot rescind, nor can the seller return due to defect except for khiyar al-shart or khiyar al-ru'ya.
Protects the minor from exploitation.
4
Memorize the Third Exception: Waqf Administrator's Transactions
A waqf administrator who buys an undervalued asset or rescinds a lease without waqf benefit cannot rescind.
Before possession, another view allows it.
5
Memorize the Fourth and Fifth Exceptions: Agents for Purchase and Salam
An agent for purchase cannot rescind by consensus. An agent for salam has a detailed ruling: per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad he can rescind but becomes liable; per Abu Yusuf he cannot after receiving price.
Key intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf point.

As for who possesses it and who does not possess it, they said: Whoever possesses the sale possesses its iqalah. Thus, iqalah of the principal (muwakkil) for what his agent sold is valid, and iqalah of the agent for sale is valid and he is liable. And we wrote in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya except in specific issues: First: The executor if he bought a house from the orphan's debtor for twenty while its value is fifty, then after collecting the debt he rescinds it, his iqalah is not valid. Second: The minor (ma'dhun) bought a slave for a thousand while its value is three thousand, his iqalah is not valid, and they (the parties) do not have the right of return for defect, unlike the right of return due to condition of option or sight; thus in Buyu' al-Qunyah. Third: The administrator of a waqf if he buys something for less than its value, his iqalah is not valid; likewise if he leases and then rescinds, and there is no benefit for the waqf, it is not permissible, as also mentioned there. In some places from it, if it is before taking possession, it is permissible, otherwise not. Fourth: The agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira') his iqalah is not valid, unlike the agent for sale (wakil bil-bay') which is valid and he is liable. Fifth: The agent for salam (wakil bil-salam) there is detail in it, and he is liable. Reflect. And what we have transmitted makes clear to you what is in the author's words regarding the narration of the statements, since from his words there is no apparent difference between the statement of Muhammad and the statement of Zufar. So the correct thing is to delete from Muhammad's statement his saying 'regarding all' because making it a sale regarding a third party is agreed upon by the three, as clarified in al-Nahr, and it is derived from what we presented. His statement: (Fifth: the agent for salam) al-Ramli said: You must reflect on what is in al-Zahiriyya, and it becomes clear if its meaning is that he possesses it on the principal according to Muhammad, and it is explicit that Abu Hanifa says he does not possess it on him, rather it is valid on himself and he is liable. Reflect. End. And al-Hamawi in his Hawashi al-Ashbah after mentioning what the author transmitted: And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The agent if he received the price does not possess iqalah by consensus. So reflect on the difference between the statement of al-Zahiriyya and Jami' al-Fusulayn, and the specification of Muhammad's statement in al-Zahiriyya is not apparent. In al-Bazzaziyya: The agent for sale possesses iqalah before or after possession, due to defect or without defect, and similar in Jami' al-Fatawa. So reflect. End. I say: The statement of Jami' al-Fusulayn is concerning after receiving the price, so it does not contradict what is in al-Zahiriyya. And what he transmitted from al-Bazzaziyya, I did not see it in iqalah, rather I saw in the tenth chapter on agency for sale from it the following text: 'Iqalah of the agent for salam and iqalah of the agent for sale are permissible according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad, unlike the agent for purchase, for he does not possess it by consensus.' End. And similar in al-Qunyah. Then he said: And he intended by iqalah of the agent for salam the agent for purchasing salam, unlike the agent for purchasing a specific item. (Regarding) iqalah of the agent for purchase on this disagreement, and he denied it, and it is the most correct. And the meaning in it is: By iqalah of the agent for sale, the price is dropped from the buyer according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and the sold item becomes incumbent on the agent, while according to Abu Yusuf the price is not dropped from the buyer at all. Al-'Isami said: If the agent sold and then rescinded before or after possession, due to defect or otherwise, it becomes incumbent on him, not the principal. Radi al-Din said: The iqalah of the principal for purchase with the seller is valid, so likewise the iqalah of the principal for sale with the buyer. End of al-Qunyah.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage focuses on the authority to perform iqalah. The general principle is that anyone who has the authority to sell also has the authority to rescind (iqalah). Therefore, a principal (muwakkil) can rescind a sale made by his agent, and an agent authorized to sell can also rescind (but becomes liable for the price if he does it without the principal's consent or without ensuring payment).

However, the author lists five exceptional cases where iqalah is not valid despite the person having the authority to sell:

1. Executor (wasi) of an orphan's estate: If the executor buys a house from a debtor of the orphan for 20 while its market value is 50, then after collecting the debt he performs iqalah, it is invalid. This is because the original sale was actually a settlement that benefited the orphan, and rescinding would revert the situation to the debtor's favor, harming the orphan.
2. Permitted minor (ma'dhun): If a minor who is allowed to trade buys a slave for 1000 when the value is 3000, his iqalah is invalid. Additionally, neither party has the right to return the item due to a hidden defect (ayb), but they do have the right to return due to an option of condition (khiyar al-shart) or option of sight (khiyar al-ru'ya). This is because the minor's iqalah is considered a new transaction that might harm his interests, and the minor is protected by the law.
3. Administrator of a waqf: If he buys something for less than its value, his iqalah is invalid. Similarly, if he leases a property and then rescinds the lease without a benefit to the waqf, it is not permissible. However, if the iqalah occurs before possession, it may be allowed in some cases.
4. Agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira'): He cannot perform iqalah because his role is solely to buy, not to sell. In contrast, an agent for sale (wakil bil-bay') can perform iqalah, but he becomes personally liable for the price.
5. Agent for salam (wakil bil-salam): There is a detailed ruling. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he can perform iqalah on behalf of the principal, but he becomes liable. According to Abu Yusuf, he cannot perform iqalah after receiving the price.

The passage ends with a discussion clarifying the Hanafi positions on who is liable and the consensus that the agent for purchase cannot rescind by consensus.

Key Terms
الوكيل بالبيع (al-wakīl bil-bay'): Agent authorized to sell property
الوكيل بالشراء (al-wakīl bil-shirā'): Agent authorized to purchase property
العبد المأذون (al-'abd al-ma'dhūn): A slave permitted by his master to engage in trade
إقالة (iqālah): Rescission of a contract by mutual agreement

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the five exceptions where iqalah is invalid according to the passage?
A) Executor's purchase from orphan's debtor
B) Agent for sale's iqalah
C) Agent for purchase's iqalah
D) Permitted minor's purchase at overvalue

Key Takeaway
The five exceptions to iqalah protect vulnerable parties: executor, minor, waqf, agent for purchase, and agent for salam (with ikhtilaf).

The General Rule and Four Clear Exceptions to Iqalah
Defining who may perform iqalah and listing four exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for iqalah (man malaka al-bay'a malaka iqalatahu) and apply the first four exceptions to determine when iqalah is invalid.

Core Idea
The right to rescind belongs to the one who owns the sale, but four exceptions protect against conflict of interest.

In this passage, the author first states the general rule: whoever has the right to execute a sale also has the right to rescind it (iqalah). Then he lists five exceptions. We will focus on the first four exceptions—involving an executor, a permitted slave, a waqf trustee, and an agent for purchase—each of which invalidates iqalah to prevent abuse of authority. Understanding these exceptions sharpens your ability to identify valid rescissions in complex transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The rule is 'man malaka al-bay'a malaka iqalatahu': whoever owns the sale owns its iqalah. This primarily refers to the principal (muwakkil) who can rescind a sale made by his agent.
The rule does not automatically grant the agent the right to rescind.
2
First exception: executor (wasi)
If the executor buys from the orphan's debtor at a low price and later rescinds after collecting the debt, the iqalah is invalid. Rescinding returns the property to the debtor, harming the orphan's estate.
Conflict of interest invalidates the rescission.
3
Second exception: permitted slave ('abd ma'dhun)
If a permitted slave buys a slave at an inflated price, his iqalah is invalid to prevent loss to the master. He also cannot return due to defect, but can return under option of stipulation or sight.
The slave's trading authority is limited; rescission would harm the master.
4
Third exception: waqf trustee (mutawalli)
If the trustee buys something undervalue, his iqalah is invalid. Similarly, if he leases then rescinds without benefit to the waqf, it is not allowed. However, if rescission occurs before delivery, it may be permissible.
The trustee must act in the best interest of the waqf.
5
Fourth exception: agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira')
The agent appointed to buy a specific item cannot rescind; only the principal can. This is by consensus.
Contrast with the agent for sale (wakil bil-bay') who can rescind but becomes liable.

داراً بعشرين وقيمتها خمسون فلما استوفى الدين أقاله لم تصح إقالته الثانية العبد المأذون اشترى غلاماً بألف وقيمته ثلاثة آلاف لا تصح إقالته ولا يملكان الرد بالعيب بخلاف الرد بخيار الشرط والرؤية؛ كذا في بيوع القنية الثالثة المتولي على الوقف إذا اشترى شيئاً بأقل من قيمته لا تصح إقالته، وكذا إذا أجر ثم أقال ولا صلاح فيها للوقف لم يجز كما فيها أيضاً، وفي بعض المواضع منها إن كان قبل القبض جازت وإلا لا . ويتضح إذا كان معناه فيملكها على الموكل في قول محمد وهو صريح في أن أبا حنيفة يقول بأنه لا يملكها عليه بل تصح على نفسه ويضمن تأمل اهـ. وقال الحموي في حواشي الأشباه بعد ذكره ما نقله المؤلف وفي جامع بعده من عيب أو من غير عيب ومثله في جامع الفتاوى فتأمل اهـ قلت كلام جامع الفصولين فيما بعد قبض الثمن فلا ينافي ما في الظهيرية وما نقله عن البزازية لم أره في إقالتها بل رأيت في العاشر في الوكالة بالبيع منها ما نصه : إقالة الوكيل بالسلم وإقالة الوكيل بالبيع جائزة عند الإمام ومحمد بخلاف الوكيل بالشراء فإنه لا يملكها إجماعاً .اهـ. ومثله في القنية. ثم قال: وأراد بإقالة الوكيل بالسلم الوكيل بشراء السلم بخلاف الوكيل بشراء العين (عن) إقالة الوكيل بالشراء على هذا الخلاف وأنكره مح وهو الأصح والمعنى فيه بإقالة الوكيل بالبيع يسقط الثمن عن المشتري عندهما ويلزم المبيع الوكيل، وعند أبي يوسف لا يسقط الثمن عن المشتري أصلاً قال في العصامي: ولو باع الوكيل ثم أقال قبل قبض أو بعده بعيب أو غير عيب لزمه دون الأمر. قال رضي الله تعالى عنه : إقالة الموكل بالشراء مع البائع لما صحت فكذلك إقالة الموكل بالبيع مع المشتري . اهـ كلام القنية .
As for who may perform iqalah and who may not: They said: Whoever owns the sale owns its iqalah. So the iqalah of the principal for what his agent sold is valid, and the iqalah of the agent for sale is valid but he becomes liable. And we have written in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyyah except in the following issues: First: If an executor buys from the debtor of the orphan a house for twenty while its value is fifty, and after collecting the debt he rescinds, his iqalah is not valid. Second: A permitted slave buys a slave for one thousand while its value is three thousand; his iqalah is not valid, and they do not have the right of return due to defect, unlike the right of return under option of stipulation or sight; as in Buyu' al-Qunyah. Third: The mutawalli (trustee) of a waqf, if he buys something for less than its value, his iqalah is not valid, and likewise if he leases then rescinds, and there is no benefit for the waqf in it, it is not permissible, as also mentioned there; and in some places, if before delivery it is allowed, otherwise not. Fourth: The agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira') cannot perform iqalah, unlike the agent for sale (wakil bil-bay'), who can, but he becomes liable. Fifth: The agent in salam (wakil bil-salam) with detail therein, and he only becomes liable, so contemplate it. His statement: (Fifth: the agent in salam) said al-Ramli: You must contemplate what is in al-Zahiriyyah, and it becomes clear if it means that according to Muhammad he can perform it on behalf of the principal, and it is explicit that Abu Hanifa says he cannot perform it on his behalf, but rather it is valid for himself and he becomes liable, so contemplate. And al-Hamawi said in Hawashi al-Ashbah after mentioning what the author reported: And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If the agent has taken the price, he does not have the right of iqalah by consensus. So contemplate the difference between the statement of al-Zahiriyyah and that of Jami' al-Fusulayn, and the specification of Muhammad's statement in al-Zahiriyyah is not apparent. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: The agent for sale can perform iqalah before or after delivery, with or without defect, and likewise in Jami' al-Fatawa, so contemplate. I say: The statement of Jami' al-Fusulayn is regarding after taking the price, so it does not contradict what is in al-Zahiriyyah. And what he reported from al-Bazzaziyyah, I did not see it concerning iqalah; rather I saw in the tenth chapter on agency in sale from it the text: The iqalah of the agent in salam and the iqalah of the agent for sale are permissible according to Imam and Muhammad, unlike the agent for purchase, for he does not have the right of iqalah by consensus. End. And similar is in al-Qunyah. Then he said: And by the iqalah of the agent in salam, he meant the agent for purchasing salam, unlike the agent for purchasing a specific item. Regarding the iqalah of the agent for purchase on this disagreement, and he denied it, and it is the most correct. The meaning thereof: By the iqalah of the agent for sale, the price is dropped from the buyer according to them, and the sold item becomes binding on the agent. According to Abu Yusuf, the price is not dropped from the buyer at all. He said in al-Isamiyyah: If the agent sells then rescinds before or after delivery, with or without defect, it is binding on him, not on the principal. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The iqalah of the principal for purchase with the seller is valid, so likewise the iqalah of the principal for sale with the buyer. End of quotation from al-Qunyah.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage discusses who has the authority to perform iqalah. The general rule is that the one who has the right to execute the sale also has the right to rescind it. However, there are five exceptions where iqalah is not allowed despite the person having the power to sell. The exceptions include: (1) an executor (wasi) who buys from the orphan's debtor at a low price and then later rescinds after collecting the debt; (2) a permitted slave (abd ma'dhun) who buys a slave at an inflated price; (3) a trustee (mutawalli) of a waqf who buys something undervalue; (4) an agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira') cannot rescind; (5) an agent in salam (wakil bil-salam) has a detailed ruling. The commentary then elaborates on the fifth exception, citing various authorities like al-Zahiriyyah, al-Ramli, al-Hamawi, al-Bazzaziyyah, and al-Qunyah, explaining that the agent in salam can rescind on behalf of the principal according to Muhammad, but according to Abu Hanifa it is allowed for himself with liability. The consensus cited is that an agent for purchase cannot rescind. The net effect is that the agent for sale can rescind and the price is dropped, but the agent becomes liable for the sold item.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasiy): Executor of a will, responsible for the orphan's property.
العبد المأذون (al-'abd al-ma'dhūn): A slave who is permitted by his master to engage in trade.
الوكيل بالشراء (al-wakīl bil-shirā'): An agent appointed to purchase a specific item on behalf of the principal.
الوكيل بالبيع (al-wakīl bil-bay'): An agent appointed to sell the principal's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first exception, why is the executor's iqalah invalid when he buys from the orphan's debtor at a low price and later rescinds?
A) Because the executor never owned the property
B) Because the executor would be returning the property to the debtor at a loss to the orphan
C) Because iqalah is never valid for executors
D) Because the debtor still owes money

Key Takeaway
The general rule for iqalah is restricted by four clear exceptions that protect parties with limited capacity from abuse.

The Agent in Salam: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Iqalah Authority
Detailing the fifth exception and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding the wakil bil-salam's right to iqalah and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The agent in salam can rescind on his own behalf with liability (Abu Hanifa) or on behalf of the principal (Muhammad), but the agent for purchase cannot rescind at all.

The fifth exception in the text deals with the agent in salam (wakil bil-salam) and sparks an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Imam Muhammad, such an agent can rescind on behalf of the principal. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he can rescind only on his own behalf, incurring liability. The author then navigates various commentaries to clarify the preferred view. This lesson walks through the disagreement and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fifth exception and the core issue
The exception is about the wakil bil-salam (agent in forward sale). The question is whether this agent can rescind the salam contract and on whose behalf.
The text states 'الوكيل بالسلم على تفصيل فيه' indicating a detailed ruling.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the agent cannot rescind on behalf of the principal; instead, the rescission is valid on himself, and he becomes liable for the price or goods.
The agent is treated as if he bought the goods for himself.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the agent can rescind on behalf of the principal, so no liability falls on the agent.
This is clearly cited from al-Zahiriyyah.
4
Note the consensus on the agent for purchase
There is consensus (ijma') that the wakil bil-shira' (agent for purchase of a specific item) cannot rescind at all.
This is stated in al-Qunyah and other sources.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq seems to favor the view that the wakil bil-salam can rescind, as per Imam and Muhammad, citing al-Qunyah which says it is permissible. The position of Abu Yusuf (price not dropped) is also mentioned but not preferred.
The mufta bihi appears to be that the agent in salam can rescind, but with the nuance that it is on himself (Abu Hanifa's view) or on behalf (Muhammad's). The later authoritative texts lean towards permissibility.

الإقالة (al-iqālah): Mutual rescission of a sale contract.

The Legal Nature of Iqalah: Dispute Among Hanafi Imams
Explaining the ikhtilaf on whether iqalah is a rescission or a new sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar regarding the legal nature of iqalah and explain the thamarah al-khilaf related to returning the price.

Core Idea
Iqalah is faskh between parties but a new sale for third parties per Abu Hanifa—a precise distinction with practical consequences.

This lesson explores the rich intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) is a rescission (faskh) or a new sale (bay'). The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the views of the four leading Hanafi imams, with nuanced conditions that change the nature of the transaction. You will learn how a single contractual term can be interpreted differently, leading to distinct rulings on issues like the return of the price and the rights of third parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four positions
List the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar on the legal nature of iqalah. Note that Abu Hanifa splits the ruling into two contexts: between the original parties and regarding third parties.
Pay attention to the textual correction: Muhammad's statement should not include 'fi haqq al-kull' because the three imams agreed it is a sale for third parties.
2
Understand the conditional exceptions
For each imam, note the scenarios where iqalah becomes impossible (e.g., item gives birth, perishes, or is repurchased at a different price) and the ruling shifts. Abu Hanifa: if faskh is impossible, iqalah is void and original sale remains; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad have their own sets.
Focus on how 'ta'azzur' (impossibility) triggers a change in the ruling for each imam.
3
Recognize the thamarah of Abu Hanifa's view
The passage states that the benefit of treating iqalah as faskh between parties appears in five issues. The first is the obligation to return the original price. This practical consequence shows why Abu Hanifa's view is preferred.
The remaining four issues are not provided here, but the method of deriving consequences is key.
4
Apply the wording distinction
Note that the ikhtilaf only applies when iqalah is uttered with its specific term. If the parties use words like faskh, radd, or tark, it is never a sale (or in some copies, never a faskh). This clarifies the scope of the dispute.
This distinction shows that the dispute is about the technical term 'iqalah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حكمها فاختلف فيه على أقوال؛ فقال الإمام الأعظم : إنها فسخ في حق المتعاقدين بيع جديد في حق ثالث. وقال أبو يوسف : إنها بيع في حق الكل. وقال محمد فسخ في حق الكل. وقال زفر : هي فسخ في حق الكل ذكر قوله في البدائع والسراج الوهاج. فالصواب أن يحذف من قول محمد قوله في حق الكل لأن جعلها بيعاً في حق الثالث اتفق عليه الثلاثة كما صرح به في النهر وهو مستفاد مما قدمناه. قوله : (هي فسخ في حق المتعاقدين بيع في حق ثالث وهذا عند أبي حنيفة إلا إن تعذر جعلها فسخاً بأن ولدت المبيعة بعد القبض أو هلك المبيع فإنها تبطل ويبقى البيع على حاله. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان قبل القبض أو بعده، وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنها فسخ قبل في البدائع. وظاهره ترجيح الإطلاق. وقال أبو يوسف: هي بيع إلا إن تعذر بأن كانت قبل القبض ففسخ إلا إن تعذرا فتبطل بأن كانت قبل القبض في المنقول بأكثر من الثمن الأول أو بأقل منه أو بجنس آخر أو بعد هلاك المبيع. وقال محمد : هي فسخ إلا إن تعذر بأن تقايلا بأكثر من الثمن الأول أو بخلاف جنسه أو ولدت المبيعة بعد القبض فبيع إلا أن تعذرا بأن كانت قبل القبض بأكثر من الثمن الأول فتبطل. والخلاف المذكور إنما هو فيما إذا وقعت بلفظها، أما بلفظ الفسخ أو الرد أو الترك فإنها لا تكون بيعاً. وفي بعض نسخ الزيلعي فإنها لا تكون فسخاً وهو سبق قلم كما لا يخفى وفي السراج الوهاج : أما إذا كانت بلفظ البيع كانت بيعاً إجماعاً كما إذا قال البائع له بعني ما اشتريت فقال بعت كان بيعاً. وفائدة كونها فسخاً في حقهما عنده تظهر في خمس مسائل : الأولى وجوب رد الثمن الأول
As for its ruling, there is disagreement according to statements: The Greatest Imam said: It is a rescission regarding the two contracting parties, a new sale regarding a third party. Abu Yusuf said: It is a sale regarding all. Muhammad said: A rescission regarding all. Zufar said: It is a rescission regarding all, as mentioned in al-Bada'i and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The correct thing is to delete from Muhammad's statement his words 'regarding all' because making it a sale regarding a third party is agreed upon by the three, as stated in al-Nahr and derived from what we have presented. His statement: (It is a rescission regarding the two contracting parties, a sale regarding a third party, and this is according to Abu Hanifa unless it becomes impossible to make it a rescission, such as if the sold item gives birth after delivery or the sold item perishes, then it becomes void and the sale remains as it was. He made it absolute, so it includes whether before or after delivery, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is a rescission before in al-Bada'i. Its apparent meaning is preference for the absolute. Abu Yusuf said: It is a sale unless it becomes impossible, such as before delivery, then a rescission, unless both become impossible, then it becomes void, such as before delivery in movable property for more than the first price or less than it or with a different genus, or after the destruction of the sold item. Muhammad said: It is a rescission unless it becomes impossible, such as if they rescind for more than the first price or with a different genus, or the sold item gives birth after delivery, then a sale, unless both become impossible, such as before delivery for more than the first price, then it becomes void. The mentioned disagreement is only when it occurs with its wording; as for the wording of rescission (faskh), return (radd), or abandonment (tark), it is not a sale. In some copies of al-Zayla'i, it is not a rescission, and that is a slip of the pen, as is not hidden. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If it is with the wording of sale, it is a sale by consensus, as if the seller says to him: 'Sell me what I bought' and he says 'I sold,' it is a sale. The benefit of it being a rescission between them according to him appears in five issues: The first is the obligation to return the first price.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal nature of iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale). It opens by stating the four positions: Abu Hanifa considers iqalah a rescission (faskh) between the two parties but a new sale (bay' jadid) regarding third parties. Abu Yusuf says it is a sale in all respects. Muhammad and Zufar say it is a rescission in all respects. The commentator then notes a textual issue: Muhammad's statement should not include 'fi haqq al-kull' because it contradicts the agreement among the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) that it is a sale vis-à-vis third parties. The passage then details the conditions under which the nature changes: if it becomes impossible to treat as rescission (e.g., the sold item gives birth or perishes after delivery), the original sale remains intact. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad have their own sets of exceptions. The disagreement only applies when iqalah is uttered with its own term; if uttered as faskh, radd, or tark, it is not a sale. The practical consequence (thamara) of Abu Hanifa's view appears in five issues, of which the first is the obligation to return the original price.

Key Terms
الإقالة (al-iqalah): Mutual rescission of a sale by agreement of both parties to cancel the transaction.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or rescission of a contract, returning both parties to their original state.
بيع جديد (bay' jadīd): A new sale where the ownership is transferred again, requiring a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first practical consequence (thamarah) of Abu Hanifa's view that iqalah is faskh between the parties, as mentioned in the passage?
A) The price is doubled.
B) The buyer must pay damages.
C) The first price must be returned.
D) The sale automatically becomes a donation.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's nuanced view on iqalah balances contractual freedom and third-party rights, making it the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Rulings on the Agent's (Wakil) Right to Perform Iqalah in Sales and Leases
Rulings on the agent's right to rescind and ownership after iqalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a wakil may validly perform iqalah in a sale or lease and explain the ownership consequences of iqalah by a co-owner agent.

Core Idea
An agent can rescind a sale only after receipt of price; a leasing agent can cancel before benefit is utilized.

In this lesson, we examine the specific rulings for an agent (wakil) when performing iqalah in sales and leases. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the timing of iqalah relative to receipt of price or benefit, and also addresses the ownership implications when a co-owner acts as an agent for sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling for wakil bil-bay'
Determine the ruling for an agent for sale performing iqalah. The default view is that iqalah is valid only after receipt of the price. Note the intra-Hanafi difference: Muhammad allows it before receipt.
2
Identify the act and ruling for wakil bil-ijarah
For an agent for lease, iqalah is valid if done before the tenant has utilized the benefit and before receiving the rental. This applies whether the rental is a specific item or a debt.
3
Analyze the trustee/executor case
A trustee or executor who sells an item above its value cannot perform iqalah, even at the original price. This prevents abuse of trust.
4
Apply the ownership principle to the co-owner case
When a co-owner sells joint property and then rescinds, the property returns to the seller's ownership, not joint ownership, so she can sell again without the other co-owner's permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوكيل بالبيع إذا أقال إذا كان بعد قبض الثمن أما قبله فيملكها في قول محمد؛ كذا في الظهيرية. وفيها . والوكيل بالإجارة إذا ناقض مع المستأجر قبل استيفاء المنفعة وقبل قبض الأجر صح سواء كان الأجر عيناً أو ديناً .اهـ. وفي فتاوى الفضلي : إذا باع المتولي أو الوصي شيئاً بأكثر من قيمته لا تجوز إقالته وإن كانت بمثل الثمن الأول .اهـ. وفي القنية : باعت ضيعة مشتركة بينها وبين ابنها البالغ وأجاز الابن البيع ثم أقالت وأجاز الابن الإقالة ثم باعتها ثانياً بغير إجازته يجوز ولا يتوقف على إجازته لأن بالإقالة يعود المبيع إلى ملك العاقد لا إلى ملك الموكل والمجيز، ودليلها السنة والإجماع وسببها الحاجة إليها ومحاسنها إزالة الغم عن النادم وتفريج الكرب من المكروب فائدة تصح إقالة الإقالة فلو تقايلا البيع ثم تقايلا الإقالة ارتفعت الإقالة وعاد البيع وكتبنا في الفوائد إلا في مسألة وهي إقالة السلم فإنها لا تقبل الإقالة كما ذكره الشارح من الدعوى من باب التحالف وفي الجوهرة : لا تصح الإقالة في النكاح والطلاق والعتاق اهـ .
The agent for sale, if he rescinds after receipt of the price, but before it, he has that right according to Muhammad; thus in al-Zahiriyyah. And in it: The agent for lease, if he cancels with the lessee before utilization of the benefit and before receipt of the rental, it is valid, whether the rental is a specific item or a debt. End. And in Fatawa al-Fadli: If a trustee or executor sells something for more than its value, his iqalah is not permissible, even if it is at the first price. End. And in al-Qunyah: A woman sold a jointly-owned estate with her adult son, and the son ratified the sale, then she rescinded and the son ratified the rescission, then she sold it a second time without his permission. This is permissible and does not depend on his permission, because by the iqalah the sold item returns to the ownership of the contracting party (the mother), not to the ownership of the principal (the son) or the one who ratified. And its proof is the Sunnah and consensus; its cause is the need for it, and its benefits include removing distress from the regretful and relieving the troubled. Benefit: The iqalah of an iqalah is valid. So if they rescind the sale, then they rescind the rescission, the rescission is lifted and the sale returns. And we have written in al-Fawa'id except in one case, which is the rescission of salam, for it does not accept rescission, as the commentator mentioned from the claim in the chapter of tahaluf. And in al-Jawharah: Iqalah is not valid in marriage, divorce, and manumission. End.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage provides specific rulings for the wakil (agent) in iqalah and explains the concept of iqalah of iqalah. It begins by stating that the agent for sale can perform iqalah after receiving the price, and according to Muhammad even before receipt. For the agent for lease (wakil bil-ijarah), cancelling the lease before the tenant has utilized the benefit and before collecting the rent is valid. A fatwa from al-Fadli states that if a trustee or executor sells at an overvalue, they cannot rescind even at the original price. A case from al-Qunyah illustrates that when a co-owner sells land jointly owned with her adult son, and the son ratifies, then she rescinds and the son also ratifies the rescission, she can resell without the son's permission because the iqalah returns the property to the seller's ownership, not the joint owner's. The passage then states that iqalah of iqalah (rescinding the rescission) is valid: if they rescind the sale and then rescind that rescission, the original sale is reinstated. However, this does not apply to salam (forward sale) contracts. Additionally, iqalah is not valid in marriage, divorce, or manumission.

Key Terms
إقالة الإقالة (iqālat al-iqālah): The act of rescinding a previous iqalah, thereby reinstating the original sale.
الوكيل بالإجارة (al-wakīl bil-ijārah): An agent appointed to lease property on behalf of the principal.
السلم (al-salam): A forward sale where payment is made in advance for future delivery of goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the mother sell the joint property a second time without her son's permission after iqalah?
A) Because the son's ratification is irrelevant
B) Because the iqalah returns ownership to her, not the son
C) Because the son already ratified the first sale
D) Because the property belonged to her entirely

Key Takeaway
An agent's iqalah is valid only under specific conditions, and iqalah by a co-owner returns ownership to the contracting party, not the joint ownership.

Iqalah al-Iqalah: Rescinding the Rescission
Ruling on rescinding the rescission and its exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on iqalah al-iqalah, identify the exceptions where it is invalid, and explain the legal effect.

Core Idea
Rescinding an iqalah reinstates the original sale, but this does not apply to salam, marriage, divorce, or manumission.

The concept of iqalah al-iqalah allows parties to return to their original positions after a rescission. However, certain contracts and personal status matters are excluded. This lesson explores the rule and its limitations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic ruling
Iqalah al-iqalah is valid and reinstates the original sale. If two parties rescind a sale (iqalah), then later they rescind that iqalah, the sale is revived.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is the Sunnah and consensus (ijma). The wisdom behind it is to remove distress and relieve the troubled.
3
List the exceptions
Iqalah al-iqalah does not apply to: salam contracts, marriage (nikah), divorce (talaq), and manumission (itq). These are excluded because of their unique legal nature.
4
Explain why exceptions exist
Salam contracts cannot be rescinded because the commodity is not yet in existence; marriage and divorce are personal status matters that require specific procedures; manumission grants freedom irrevocably.

Source Text
