The General Principle of Including Expenses in Murabahah Capital
Enumeration of includable expenses with legal justification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle for including expenses in murabahah capital and apply it to examples such as dyeing, carriage, and construction costs.

Core Idea
Any expense that increases the item or its value may be added, based on custom.

In murabahah, the seller discloses cost plus profit. But which costs can be included? The Hanafi school provides a clear principle: any expense that enhances the good or its value is includable, grounded in merchant custom. This lesson unpacks the rule and the key examples given by classical jurists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The seller adding expenses to capital in murabahah is permissible (ja'iz) as per the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the principle
The passage states two bases: custom (urf) and the rule that anything increasing the item or its value is attached to capital.
Al-urf is a recognized source in Hanafi commercial law.
3
Work through the examples
Dyeing increases the physical item; carriage increases value due to location change. Both are includable.
The text also includes embroidery, twisting, and driving sheep.
4
Extend to other expenses
Commentary adds washing, sewing, plastering, well-digging, etc., all fitting the same principle.
Exception: wasteful food for the item is not included.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وله أن يضم إلى رأس المال أجر القصار والصبغ والطراز والفتل وحمل الطعام وسوق الغنم) لأن العرف جاز بالحاق هذه الأشياء برأس المال في عادة التجار ولأن كل ما يزيد في المبيع أو قيمته يلحق به هذا هو الأصل وما عددناه بهذه الصفة لأن الصبغ وأخواته يزيد في العين والحمل يزيد في القيمة إذ القيمة تختلف باختلاف المكان. والطراز بكسر الطاء وتخفيف الراء العلم في الثوب ؛ كذا في المغرب. والفتل هو ما يصنع بأطراف الثياب بحرير أو كتان من فتلت الحبل أفتله أطلق الصبغ فشمل الأسود وغيره كما أطلق حمل الطعام فشمل البر والبحر، وقيد بالأجرة لأنه لو فعل شيئاً من ذلك بیده يضمه، وكذا لو تطوع متطوع بهذه أو بإعارة ودل كلامه على أنه يضم أجرة الغسل والخياطة ونفقة تجصيص الدار وطي البئر وكراء الأنهار والقناة والمسناة والكراب وكسج الكروم وسقيها والزرع وغرس الأشجار. وفي المحيط وغيره يضم طعام المبيع إلا ما كان سرفاً وزيادة فلا يضم وكسوته وكراءه وأجرة المخزن الذي يوضع فيه ، وأما أجرة السمسار والدلال فقال الشارح: إن كانت مشروطة في العقد تضم وإلا فأكثرهم على عدم الضم في الأول ولا تضم أجرة الدلال بالإجماع اهـ. وهو تسامح فإن أجرة الأول تضم في ظاهر الرواية والتفصيل المذكور قويلة هو الدال على مكان السلعة وصاحبها والدلال هو المصاحب للسلعة غالباً
He said: 'He may add to the capital the wage of the closer, dyeing, embroidery, twisting, carriage of food, and driving of sheep.' Because custom allows attaching these things to the capital in the practice of merchants, and because everything that increases the sold item or its value is attached to it; this is the principle. What we have enumerated are of this description because dyeing and its likes increase the physical item, and carriage increases the value since value differs by location. Al-Tiraz (with kasr of ta and tashdid of ra) is the mark on the cloth; as in al-Mughrib. Al-Fatl is what is made at the edges of garments with silk or flax, from fatl al-habl (twisting the rope). He made dyeing general, so it includes black and others, just as he made carriage of food general, so it includes land and sea. And he restricted it to wage because if he did any of that with his own hand, he includes it. Similarly, if a volunteer volunteered these or by lending. And his words indicate that he includes the wage of washing, sewing, expense of plastering the house, digging the well, renting of canals, aqueducts, dam, bridge, covering of vineyards, watering them, cultivation, and planting trees. And in al-Muhit and others, he includes the food of the sold item except what is wasteful and excessive, so he does not include it, and its clothing, its rent, and the rent of the storehouse where it is placed. As for the wage of the simsar and dallal, the commentator said: if it is stipulated in the contract, it is included; otherwise, most are of the opinion that it is not included in the first, and the wage of the dallal is not included by consensus. End quote. And this is lenient, for the wage of the first (simsar) is included in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), and the mentioned detail is a saying. He is the one who indicates the place of the commodity and its owner, and the dallal is the one who accompanies the commodity mostly.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, listing expenses that can be added to the capital cost in a murabahah sale. The principle is that any expenditure that increases the physical item or its value may be included. The text gives specific examples: wages for a fuller (qassar), dyeing, embroidery, twisting, carriage of food, and driving sheep. These are justified by custom (urf) and the fact that they enhance the good. The commentary defines two terms: tiraz (a mark on cloth) and fatl (twisting at garment edges). It extends the list to washing, sewing, construction costs, etc. However, food for the item is added only if not excessive. For the wages of a simsar (agent) and dallal (broker), the commentator notes a difference: if stipulated in the contract, they are included; otherwise, simsar's wage is included in the established narration (zahir al-riwayah), while dallal's wage is not included by consensus. The passage ends with definitions distinguishing the simsar (who points to the goods and owner) from the dallal (who accompanies the goods).

Key Terms
السمسار (al-simsār): An intermediary who points out the goods and their owner
الدلال (al-dallāl): A broker who accompanies the goods and markets them
عرف (ʿurf): Customary practice of merchants

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a basis for including expenses? a) Custom of merchants b) The expense increases the physical item c) The expense is paid to a relative d) The expense increases the value
A) Custom of merchants
B) The expense increases the physical item
C) The expense is paid to a relative
D) The expense increases the value

Key Takeaway
In murabahah, only expenses that enhance the item or its value may be added to capital, grounded in custom.

The Wage of Intermediaries: Simsar vs. Dallal in Murabahah
Clarification of a disputed point regarding agent and broker fees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a simsar and a dallal, and explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on including their wages in capital.

Core Idea
Simsar's wage is included in capital in the reliable narration; dallal's wage is excluded by consensus unless stipulated.

The passage ends with an important nuance: not all intermediary costs are treated equally. The simsar (who merely points out the goods) and the dallal (who actively markets them) have different rulings. Understanding this distinction avoids a common pitfall in murabahah calculations.

Guided Path
1
Define simsar and dallal
The passage defines: simsar indicates the place of the commodity and its owner; dallal accompanies the commodity and markets it.
These definitions are crucial for applying the correct ruling.
2
State the consensus on dallal
The wage of the dallal is not included in capital by consensus (ijma') unless stipulated in the contract.
This is strong authority.
3
State the dispute on simsar
Most Hanafi scholars say simsar's wage is not included unless stipulated. However, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) holds that it is included even without stipulation.
The commentator notes this is the stronger view.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The commentator leans toward including simsar's wage based on the apparent narration, which is the relied-upon position.
Thus, simsar's wage should be included in capital in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وله أن يضم إلى رأس المال أجر القصار والصبغ والطراز والفتل وحمل الطعام وسوق الغنم) لأن العرف جاز بالحاق هذه الأشياء برأس المال في عادة التجار ولأن كل ما يزيد في المبيع أو قيمته يلحق به هذا هو الأصل وما عددناه بهذه الصفة لأن الصبغ وأخواته يزيد في العين والحمل يزيد في القيمة إذ القيمة تختلف باختلاف المكان. والطراز بكسر الطاء وتخفيف الراء العلم في الثوب ؛ كذا في المغرب. والفتل هو ما يصنع بأطراف الثياب بحرير أو كتان من فتلت الحبل أفتله أطلق الصبغ فشمل الأسود وغيره كما أطلق حمل الطعام فشمل البر والبحر، وقيد بالأجرة لأنه لو فعل شيئاً من ذلك بیده يضمه، وكذا لو تطوع متطوع بهذه أو بإعارة ودل كلامه على أنه يضم أجرة الغسل والخياطة ونفقة تجصيص الدار وطي البئر وكراء الأنهار والقناة والمسناة والكراب وكسج الكروم وسقيها والزرع وغرس الأشجار. وفي المحيط وغيره يضم طعام المبيع إلا ما كان سرفاً وزيادة فلا يضم وكسوته وكراءه وأجرة المخزن الذي يوضع فيه ، وأما أجرة السمسار والدلال فقال الشارح: إن كانت مشروطة في العقد تضم وإلا فأكثرهم على عدم الضم في الأول ولا تضم أجرة الدلال بالإجماع اهـ. وهو تسامح فإن أجرة الأول تضم في ظاهر الرواية والتفصيل المذكور قويلة هو الدال على مكان السلعة وصاحبها والدلال هو المصاحب للسلعة غالباً
He said: 'He may add to the capital the wage of the closer, dyeing, embroidery, twisting, carriage of food, and driving of sheep.' Because custom allows attaching these things to the capital in the practice of merchants, and because everything that increases the sold item or its value is attached to it; this is the principle. What we have enumerated are of this description because dyeing and its likes increase the physical item, and carriage increases the value since value differs by location. Al-Tiraz (with kasr of ta and tashdid of ra) is the mark on the cloth; as in al-Mughrib. Al-Fatl is what is made at the edges of garments with silk or flax, from fatl al-habl (twisting the rope). He made dyeing general, so it includes black and others, just as he made carriage of food general, so it includes land and sea. And he restricted it to wage because if he did any of that with his own hand, he includes it. Similarly, if a volunteer volunteered these or by lending. And his words indicate that he includes the wage of washing, sewing, expense of plastering the house, digging the well, renting of canals, aqueducts, dam, bridge, covering of vineyards, watering them, cultivation, and planting trees. And in al-Muhit and others, he includes the food of the sold item except what is wasteful and excessive, so he does not include it, and its clothing, its rent, and the rent of the storehouse where it is placed. As for the wage of the simsar and dallal, the commentator said: if it is stipulated in the contract, it is included; otherwise, most are of the opinion that it is not included in the first, and the wage of the dallal is not included by consensus. End quote. And this is lenient, for the wage of the first (simsar) is included in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), and the mentioned detail is a saying. He is the one who indicates the place of the commodity and its owner, and the dallal is the one who accompanies the commodity mostly.

Commentary
This passage comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, listing expenses that can be added to the capital cost in a murabahah sale. The principle is that any expenditure that increases the physical item or its value may be included. The text gives specific examples: wages for a fuller (qassar), dyeing, embroidery, twisting, carriage of food, and driving sheep. These are justified by custom (urf) and the fact that they enhance the good. The commentary defines two terms: tiraz (a mark on cloth) and fatl (twisting at garment edges). It extends the list to washing, sewing, construction costs, etc. However, food for the item is added only if not excessive. For the wages of a simsar (agent) and dallal (broker), the commentator notes a difference: if stipulated in the contract, they are included; otherwise, simsar's wage is included in the established narration (zahir al-riwayah), while dallal's wage is not included by consensus. The passage ends with definitions distinguishing the simsar (who points to the goods and owner) from the dallal (who accompanies the goods).

Key Terms
السمسار (al-simsār): An intermediary who points out the goods and their owner
الدلال (al-dallāl): A broker who accompanies the goods and markets them
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or well-known narration from Imam Muhammad's six books

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the dallal's wage? a) Included by consensus b) Excluded by consensus c) Included only if stipulated d) Disputed
A) Included by consensus
B) Excluded by consensus
C) Included only if stipulated
D) Disputed

Key Takeaway
Simsar's wage is included in murabahah capital per the stronger narration; dallal's wage is excluded by consensus unless stipulated.

Murabahah on a Numbered Price: Truthfulness Required
Expansion of a ruling on murabahah with a written price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on murabahah when the seller writes a price on the item and identify the condition of truthfulness that governs its validity.

Core Idea
Murabahah on a written price is valid only if the seller is truthful about the number.

When a seller acquires an item through gift or inheritance, they may sell it by murabahah by stating a written number or value. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that such a sale is permissible provided the seller is truthful. It also highlights an apparent disagreement between later Hanafi texts on whether the phrase 'its value is such' may be used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The seller acquired the item without purchase (e.g., by gift, inheritance, or bequest). He writes a number on it and then sells by murabahah referring to that number.
This scenario distinguishes from murabahah where the seller states the original purchase price.
2
Understand the method of stating the price
The seller may say 'its number is such' or 'its value is such'. The term 'number' refers to a written amount that may equal or exceed the actual value.
The commentator clarifies that the number should represent the true value.
3
Analyze the condition of truthfulness
The sale is valid only if the seller is truthful about the number/value. If the buyer loses due to the number being higher than true value, it is his own ignorance, not the seller's betrayal.
Truthfulness is the key condition derived from the commentator's emphasis on 'wa huwa ṣādiq'.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi contradiction
The passage notes that Fath al-Qadir permits saying 'its value is such', while al-Nihayah prohibits it. This is an unresolved difference within the Hanafi school.
The commentator does not resolve the contradiction but presents both positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكذا إذا رقم على الثوب الخ) صدر هذا الكلام يوهم أنه يقول قام علي بكذا فكان الأولى أن يقول «وأما إذا رقم الثوب الخ وعبارة الفتح : وكذا لو ملكه بهبة أو إرث أو وصية وقوم قيمته ثم باعه مرابحة يجوز. وصورة هذه المسألة أن يقول قيمته كذا أو رقمه كذا فأرابحك على القيمة أو رقمه، ومعنى الرقم أن يكتب على الثوب المشتري مقداراً سواء كان قدر الثمن أو أزيد ثم يرابحه عليه وهو إذا قال رقمه كذا وهو صادق لم يكن خائناً فإن غبن المشتري فيه فمن قبل جهله .اهـ. وظاهره أن الرقم يكون بالقيمة لا بأكثر وإن زادت على الثمن ويدل عليه قوله وهو صادق وإلا فما وجه اشتراط صدقه؟ وحينئذ فيجوز أن يقول رقمه كذا أو قيمته كذا وينافيه ما مر عن النهاية من أنه لا يقول قام علي بكذا ولا قيمته
He said: 'Similarly, if he numbers on the cloth etc.' The beginning of this statement gives the impression that he says 'it cost me such-and-such', so it would have been better to say 'As for when he numbers the cloth...'. And the wording of al-Fath: 'Similarly, if he owned it by gift, inheritance, or bequest, and evaluated its value, then sold it by murabahah, it is permissible. The picture of this issue is that he says: its value is such, or its number is such, and I sell with murabahah to you on the value or its number. The meaning of numbering is that he writes on the cloth a certain amount, whether equal to the price or more, then sells with murabahah on it. And if he says: its number is such, and he is truthful, then he is not a betrayer; if the buyer is cheated in it, it is due to his ignorance.' End quote. And its apparent meaning is that the number is according to the value, not more, even if it exceeds the price, and his statement 'and he is truthful' indicates this, otherwise what is the reason for stipulating his truthfulness? Then in that case, it is permissible for him to say 'its number is such' or 'its value is such', and it contradicts what passed from al-Nihayah that he should not say 'it cost me such' nor 'its value'.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of selling a item by murabahah based on a price written (رقم) on it, such as when the seller acquired it through gift or inheritance and writes a value. The ruling from Fath al-Qadir states that if he says 'its value is such' or 'its number is such' and is truthful, the sale is valid, and any loss to the buyer is due to his own ignorance. The commentary clarifies that the numbered amount must represent the true value, not an inflated figure, as indicated by the condition of truthfulness. This appears to contradict a previous statement from al-Nihayah that one should not say 'it cost me such' or 'its value'. The passage ends with this apparent contradiction.

Key Terms
الرقم (al-raqm): A written number on the item indicating its price or value
قام علي (qāma ʿalayya): The phrase 'it cost me' used in murabahah to state capital

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir, what is the condition for the validity of murabahah based on a numbered price (رقم)?
A) The number must be greater than the actual value
B) The seller must be truthful about the number
C) The buyer must inspect the item
D) The number must be written in Arabic

Key Takeaway
Murabahah based on a numbered price or value is valid only if the seller is truthful about that number/value.

Adding Expenses to Cost Price in Murabaha
Ruling with proof on permissible additions to murabaha cost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for which expenses may be added to the cost price in a murabaha sale, and justify the inclusion using custom (urf) and analogy (qiyas).

Core Idea
Only expenses that increase the good or its value may be added to the cost price in murabaha.

In a murabaha sale, the seller must disclose the true cost price. But what counts as 'cost'? This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that not all expenses incurred on an item can be added; only those that increase the item itself or its market value are includable. The Hanafi school relies on the custom of merchants and a strong analogical reasoning to draw this line. Let's examine the principle, the enumerated expenses, and the critical distinction between the simsar and dallal brokers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is including certain expenses in the stated cost price for a murabaha sale. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) and in fact required for truthful disclosure. Identify the key term: 'wa lahu an yadumma' (he may include).
The ruling is not that the seller must include; but if he does not, his disclosure is incomplete.
2
Locate the Dalil
The passage gives two proofs: custom ('urf al-tujjar) and a rational principle (kullu ma yazid fi al-mabi' aw qimatihi yalhaqu bihi). Identify these as the basis.
Custom is a secondary source in Hanafi fiqh for mu'amalat.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (Legal Link)
Custom has allowed adding these expenses. The rational principle explains why: dye increases the substance, transport increases value by location. Connect each listed expense to either 'increase in substance' or 'increase in value'.
This is a combination of urf and qiyas; the qiyas is from dye to transport.
4
Note the Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf on Simsar
The passage states that the simsar's wage (if not stipulated) is excluded by some, but the author of the sharh rejects that as weak, affirming inclusion as per zahir al-riwaya. The dallal's wage is never included by consensus.
Know the role difference: simsar indicates location, dallal accompanies the goods.
5
Apply to a New Case
Test the principle: a tailor sews a garment after purchase. Is his wage includable? The text includes khiyata (sewing) explicitly, so yes. What about the seller's own travel food? Not increasing the item, so no.
Always check: does the expense increase the physical good or its value?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المرابحة والتولية
إلى رأس المال أجر القصار والصبغ والطراز والفتل وحمل الطعام وسوق الغنم ويقول قام علي المقبوض ، وكذا لو ولاهما رجلاً جازت التولية في المقبوض . ولو اشترى جاريتين بألف درهم وقبضهما وباع أحدهما ثم ولاهما رجلاً فالمولى بالخيار إن شاء أخذ التي لم تبع بحصتها وإن شاء ترك إذا لم يعلم ببيع أحدهما، وكذلك لو أشرك فيهما جازت الشركة في نصف التي لم تبع وإن لم يبع أحدهما ولكنه أعتق أحدهما أو ماتت ثم ولاهما رجلاً أو أشركه فيهما جاز في الأمة والحية منهما ؛ كذا في الظهيرية وفي السراج الوهاج : لو كان مثلياً فرابح على بعضه جاز كقفيز من قفيزين لعدم التفاوت بخلاف القيمي وتمام تفريعه في شرح المجمع. وفي المحيط : وإن كان ثوباً ونحوه لا يبيع جزءاً منه معيناً لأن الثمن ينقسم عليه باعتبار القيمة وإن باع جزءاً شائعاً جاز وقيل يفسد البيع.
.
У
قوله : ( وله أن يضم إلى رأس المال أجر القصار والصبغ والطراز والفتل وحمل الطعام وسوق الغنم) لأن العرف جاز بالحاق هذه الأشياء برأس المال في عادة التجار ولأن كل ما يزيد في المبيع أو قيمته يلحق به هذا هو الأصل وما عددناه بهذه الصفة لأن الصبغ وأخواته يزيد في العين والحمل يزيد في القيمة إذ القيمة تختلف باختلاف المكان. والطراز بكسر الطاء وتخفيف الراء العلم في الثوب ؛ كذا في المغرب. والفتل هو ما يصنع بأطراف الثياب بحرير أو كتان من فتلت الحبل أفتله أطلق الصبغ فشمل الأسود وغيره كما أطلق حمل الطعام فشمل البر والبحر، وقيد بالأجرة لأنه لو فعل شيئاً من ذلك بیده يضمه، وكذا لو تطوع متطوع بهذه أو بإعارة ودل كلامه على أنه يضم أجرة الغسل والخياطة ونفقة تجصيص الدار وطي البئر وكراء الأنهار والقناة والمسناة والكراب وكسج الكروم وسقيها والزرع وغرس الأشجار. وفي المحيط وغيره يضم طعام المبيع إلا ما كان سرفاً وزيادة فلا يضم وكسوته وكراءه وأجرة المخزن الذي يوضع فيه ، وأما أجرة السمسار والدلال فقال الشارح: إن كانت مشروطة في العقد تضم وإلا فأكثرهم على عدم الضم في الأول ولا تضم أجرة الدلال بالإجماع اهـ. وهو تسامح فإن أجرة الأول تضم في ظاهر الرواية والتفصيل المذكور قويلة
هو الدال على مكان السلعة وصاحبها والدلال هو المصاحب للسلعة غالباً
Book of Sales, Chapter on Murabaha and Tawliya. Into the capital are included the wages of the fuller, dyeing, embroidery, twisting, transport of food, and driving of sheep, and he says 'it cost me' (qama alayya) on the received [item]. Likewise, if he made them tawliya to a person, tawliya is valid on the received [item]. If he bought two slave girls for a thousand dirhams, took possession of them, sold one, then made them tawliya to a person, then the assignee has the option: if he wishes he takes the unsold one for its share, and if he wishes he may leave, provided he did not know of the sale of one. Similarly, if he made a partnership in them, partnership is valid in half of the unsold one. If he did not sell either but freed one or it died, then made them tawliya to a person or made him a partner, it is valid in the one that remains alive; thus in al-Zahiriyya. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if it is a mithli item and he makes a profit on some of it, it is valid, like a qafiz from two qafizes because of no disparity, unlike a qimi item; and its full furu' are in Sharh al-Majma'. In al-Muhit: if it is a cloth and the like, he may not sell a specific part of it because the price is divided over it according to value, but if he sells an undivided part it is valid, and it is said the sale is invalid. He said: (He may include in the capital the wages of the fuller, etc.) Because custom has allowed attaching these things to the capital in the custom of merchants, and because everything that increases the sold item or its value is attached to it; this is the principle, and what we have enumerated is of this description because dye and its like increase the substance, and transport increases the value since value varies with location. Al-Tiraz (with kasr al-ta' and takhfif al-ra') is the mark on the cloth; thus in al-Maghrib. Al-Fatl is what is made at the ends of garments with silk or linen, from 'fataltu al-habla a'futulu'. He [the author] used the term 'dyeing' generally, so it includes black and other colors, just as he generally used 'transport of food' to include land and sea. He restricted it to wages because if he does any of that with his own hand, he includes it [in capital]. Likewise, if a volunteer does it via gift or loan. His words indicate that he includes wages for washing, sewing, the expenses of plastering a house, digging a well, rent of rivers, canals, conduits, dams, digging of vines, their irrigation, cultivation, and planting of trees. In al-Muhit and elsewhere, the food of the sold item is included except that which is wasteful and excessive, then it is not included; and its covering, rent, and the rent of the storage. As for the wage of the simsar and dallal, the sharh said: if they were stipulated in the contract then they are included; if not, most say they are not included for the former, and the wage of the dallal is not included by consensus. But this is lenient, for the wage of the former is included in the zahir al-riwaya, and the aforementioned detail [is] weak. The simsar is the one who indicates the place of the commodity and its owner, and the dallal is the one who accompanies the commodity usually.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on what expenses may be added to the cost price (ra's al-mal) in a murabaha sale. The core principle, as stated in the sharh, is that anything that increases the sold item itself or its value may be added to the capital. This is based on the custom of merchants and rational reasoning (kullu ma yazid fi al-mabi' aw qimatihi yalhaqu bihi). The matn enumerates specific wages: fuller (qassar), dyeing (sibgh), embroidery (tiraz), twisting (fatl), transport of food (haml al-ta'am), and driving sheep (saq al-ghanam). The sharh explains that these are included because they either increase the physical substance (al-'ayn) like dyeing, or increase the value (al-qima) like transport. The autho also mentions that if the merchant does the work himself, he does not add wages, but if a volunteer does it, the equivalent wage is added. The phrase 'wa yaqulu qama alayya' indicates that the seller must truthfully state the cost price, not a false statement. The passage also discusses rulings on tawliya and partnership when purchasing multiple items, and clarifies that selling a specified part of a non-fungible item is invalid, but selling an undivided share is valid. The discussion of simsar and dallal wages: the simsar's wage, if stipulated, is included; if not, the soundest position (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is included, but the dallal's wage is never included by consensus. The final line distinguishes the roles: simsar indicates the location, dallal accompanies the goods.

Key Terms
المرابحة (al-murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost price and adds an agreed profit.
السمسار (al-simsar): A broker who indicates the location of the commodity and its owner.
الدلال (al-dallal): A broker who accompanies the commodity (e.g., to the market).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following expenses CAN be added to the cost price in a murabaha sale?
A) The seller's own food expenses while traveling to buy the item
B) The wage of a tailor who altered the cloth after purchase
C) The rent of a storage room where the item was kept
D) The wage of a dallal (accompanying broker) by consensus

Key Takeaway
In murabaha, only expenses that increase the good or its value may be added to the cost, based on custom (urf) and analogy (qiyas); the simsar's wage is included, but the dallal's is not.

Expenses Not Added to Capital: Custom as the Decisive Factor
Ruling on expenses not included in murabaha capital with custom as proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which expenses are not added to capital in murabaha and explain the role of custom (urf) in determining inclusion.

Core Idea
Expenses that do not directly increase market value per custom are not added to the cost in murabaha.

In a murabaha sale, the seller must honestly declare the cost price. But which expenses can be added? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that certain expenditures—like teaching a slave or hiring a shepherd—are excluded. The key is not whether value increases, but whether the custom of merchants includes such expenses. Understanding this principle prevents invalid contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
First, note the three explicit examples: shepherd's wage, teacher's fee, and guard-house rent. The matn states they are not added. Recognize that this is a negative ruling: these expenses belong to a category that must be excluded.
The ruling is based on 'adam al-urf (absence of custom).
2
Analyze the Proof: Custom (Urf)
The commentary explicitly cites lack of custom as the basis. Understand that urf is a legitimate source in Hanafi mu'amalat. Here, the prevailing custom among merchants is to treat these expenses as separate, not part of the capital.
The proof is zanni (speculative) but sufficient for mu'amalat.
3
Examine the Rationale for Teaching (Ta'lim)
Teaching increases the slave's value, but the increase is attributed to the slave's innate ability (hadaqah), not the teaching expenditure. The teacher's fee is like a condition (shart) for the increase, not a cause (sabab). However, the text notes that if custom were otherwise, it would be added.
This is a nuance: the underlying cause is the slave's capacity, not the teaching.
4
Note the Extended List of Excluded Expenses
The sharh extends the ruling to doctor, trainer, vet, blood money, cost of retrieving a runaway slave, cupping, circumcision, and even the owner's own living expenses. All are excluded due to lack of custom or rarity (nudrah).
The principle is consistent: only expenses with manifest custom (urf zahir) are added.
5
Apply the Custom Principle
Finally, understand that custom can vary by time and place. If in a particular market it is customary to include teaching expenses, then it would be allowed. The ruling is not absolute but tied to urf. This flexibility is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh.
The mufta bihi is to follow the prevailing custom of honest merchants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يضم أجرة الراعي والتعليم وكراء بيت الحفظ) لعدم العرف بإلحاقه. أطلق في التعليم فشمل تعليم العبد صناعة أو قرآناً أو علماً أو شعراً أو غناء أو عربية قالوا : لأن ثبوت الزيادة لمعنى في العبد وهو حذاقته فلم يكن ما أنفقه على المعلم موجباً للزيادة في المالية، ولا يخفى ما فيه إذ لا شك في حصول الزيادة بالتعلم ولا شك أنه مسبب عن التعليم عادة وكونه بمساعدة القابلية في المتعلم هو كقابلية الثوب للصبغ نسبته إلى التعليم فهو شرط علة عادية والقابلية شرط وفي المبسوط : أضاف نفي ضم المنفق في التعليم إلى أنه ليس فيه عرف ظاهر حتى لو كان فيه عرف ظاهر يلحق برأس المال؛ في فتح القدير. وأشار المؤلف إلى أنه لا يضم أجرة الطبيب والرائض والبيطار والداء في الجناية وجعل الآبق لندرته فلا يلحق بالسابق لأنه لا عرف في النادر والحجامة والختان لعدم العرف، وكذا لا يضم نفقة نفسه وكراءه ولا مهر العبد ولا يحط مهر الأمة لزوجها، والذي يؤخذ في الطريق من الظلم لا يضم إلا في موضع جرت العادة فيه بينهم بالضم .
His saying: (The wage of the shepherd, the teacher, and the rent of the guard house are not included) due to the lack of custom of attaching it. He used 'teaching' generally, so it includes teaching a slave a craft, the Quran, knowledge, poetry, singing, or Arabic. They said: because the increase is due to a quality in the slave, namely his skill, so what he spent on the teacher is not the cause of the increase in monetary value. And it is not hidden what is in this [argument], for there is no doubt that increase occurs through learning, and there is no doubt that it is normally caused by teaching; the fact that it is assisted by the capacity of the learner is like the capacity of the cloth for dye; the relation to teaching is that it is a condition of the customary cause, and capacity is a condition. In al-Mabsut: he added the negation of including the expenditure on teaching to the point that there is no manifest custom; so if there were a manifest custom, it would be added to the capital; in Fath al-Qadir. The author indicated that the wage of the doctor, the trainer, the vet, and the blood money in a tort, and the cost of returning a runaway slave due to its rarity are not included, because there is no custom in rare matters; also cupping and circumcision due to lack of custom. Similarly, his own maintenance and rent, the dower of a slave, and the dower of a female slave for her husband are not deducted. What is taken on the road unjustly is not included unless it is the custom among them to include it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage details which expenses are NOT added to the capital in a murabaha sale, based on the matn 'wa la yudammu ujrat al-ra'i wa al-ta'lim wa kira' bayt al-hifz'. The rationale is the absence of custom ('adam al-urf) in including them. The sharh elaborates on 'teaching' (ta'lim): it covers any kind of teaching given to a slave. While teaching increases the slave's skill, the increase is attributed to the slave's innate ability, not the teaching expenditure—thus it is not added. However, there is a subtle argument: if custom (urf) were established, it would be added, as per al-Mabsut. The author also lists other non-added expenses: doctor's wage, trainer, vet, blood money (for injuries to the slave), cost of retrieving a runaway slave (due to rarity), cupping and circumcision (no custom). Also not added: the owner's own living expenses and rent, the dower of a slave or female slave. Unjustly extorted payments on the road are not added unless customarily included. The overall principle is that only expenses that customarily increase the value and are commonly included by merchants are added.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): Prevailing custom among merchants, used as a basis for including or excluding expenses in murabaha.
التعليم (al-ta'lim): Teaching a slave a craft or knowledge; the expense is not added because the increase is due to the slave's capacity, not the teaching itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the wage of a teacher not added to the capital in murabaha according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because learning does not increase the slave's value at all
B) Because the increase is due to the slave's innate capacity, not the teaching expenditure, and there is no custom
C) Because teaching is considered a form of worship, not trade
D) Because the teacher is not a merchant

Key Takeaway
Expenses are added to murabaha capital only if they customarily increase market value and are commonly included by merchants.

Remedies for Dishonesty in Murabaha and Tawliya
Intra-Hanafi dispute on buyer's remedy after seller's dishonesty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the remedies for dishonesty in murabaha and tawliya according to the three Hanafi masters and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Dishonesty in price breaks a murabaha differently than a tawliya — the name of the contract dictates the remedy.

When a seller misrepresents the cost price in a trust-based sale (murabaha or tawliya), the buyer's legal remedy varies depending on which Hanafi imam's view is followed. This lesson unpacks the three-way dispute between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, each offering a distinct reasoning based on the nature of the contract name and the role of the first price.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the source text and list the remedy proposed by each imam for murabaha and tawliya separately.
Abu Hanifa differentiates between the two contracts; the Sahibayn treat them similarly.
2
Analyze the reasoning of Muhammad
Muhammad argues that contract names are like desirable attributes (e.g., safety). Explain why this leads to an option (takhyir) in both contracts.
Focus on the phrase 'tawliya and murabaha are promotion and inducement'.
3
Analyze the reasoning of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf stresses 'building on the first price'. Explain how deduction (hatt) from capital (tawliya) or capital+profit (murabaha) follows from this.
Note that the amount deducted differs between the two contracts according to Abu Yusuf.
4
Analyze the reasoning of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the two contracts: in tawliya, failing to deduct changes the nature; in murabaha, the name remains despite profit difference. Explain this logic.
The key is 'taghayyur al-tasarruf' (change of transaction) vs remaining a valid murabaha.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For a given factual scenario, state what each imam's ruling would be and highlight the difference in outcome.
This step consolidates the legal distinction into real-world application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن خان في مرابحة أخذ بكل ثمنه أو رده وحط في التولية) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف يحط فيهما . وقال محمد يخير فيهما . لمحمد أن الاعتبار للتسمية لكونه معلوماً والتولية والمرابحة ترويج وترغيب فتكون وصفاً مرغوباً فيه كوصف السلامة فيتخير لفواته. ولأبي يوسف أن الأصل فيه كونه تولية ومرابحة ولهذا ينعقد بقوله وليتك بالثمن الأول أو بعتك مرابحة على الثمن الأول إذا كان معلوماً فلا بد من البناء على الأول وذلك بالحط غير أنه يحط في التولية قدر الخيانة من رأس المال، وفي المرابحة منه ومن الربح. ولأبي حنيفة أنه لو لم يحط في التولية لا تبقى تولية لأنه يزيد على الثمن الأول فتغير التصرف فتعين الحط، وفي المرابحة لو لم يحط تبقى مرابحة وإن كان يتفاوت الربح فلا يتغير
His saying: (If he cheats in murabaha, he [the buyer] takes it at its full price or returns it, and in tawliya he deducts.) This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: he deducts in both. Muhammad said: he has an option in both. For Muhammad, consideration is given to the name because it is known, and tawliya and murabaha are promotion and inducement, so they become a desirable attribute like the attribute of safety, so he may choose due to its loss. For Abu Yusuf, the basis is that it is tawliya and murabaha, and for this reason it is concluded by his saying 'I give you tawliya at the first price' or 'I sell you murabaha at the first price' if it is known, so it must be built on the first, and that is by deduction, except that he deducts in tawliya the amount of cheating from the capital, and in murabaha from the capital and the profit. For Abu Hanifa, if he does not deduct in tawliya, it would not remain tawliya because it would exceed the first price, so the transaction changes, so deduction is determined; and in murabaha, if he does not deduct, it remains murabaha even though the profit differs, so it does not change [the name].
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the remedy when a seller is dishonest (khana) in a murabaha or tawliya sale. The matn states the ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa: in murabaha, the buyer can either take the item at the full (dishonest) price or return it; in tawliya, the buyer deducts the cheated amount. Abu Yusuf differs: in both cases, the buyer deducts the cheated amount from the price. Muhammad differs again: in both cases, the buyer has an option (takhyir): either take at the dishonest price or return the item. The reasoning: Muhammad argues that the names 'murabaha' and 'tawliya' are known attributes that induce the buyer, like the attribute of safety; if lost, the buyer may annul. Abu Yusuf argues that the nature of the contracts requires building on the first price, so deduction is necessary; the only difference is what is deducted: in tawliya, only the capital; in murabaha, both capital and profit. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: in tawliya, not deducting would change the nature of the contract (since the price would exceed the first price), so deduction is required; in murabaha, the contract name remains even if the profit amount changes, so the buyer may take at the stated price or return. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is typically Abu Hanifa's, but all three positions are recorded.

Key Terms
الخيانة (al-khiyanah): Dishonesty by the seller in stating a higher cost price than actual.
التولية (al-tawliyah): Sale where the seller transfers ownership at exactly the cost price, without profit.
الحط (al-hatt): Reduction of the price by the amount of dishonesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the remedy for a buyer when the seller cheats in a murabaha sale?
A) The buyer can only deduct the cheated amount
B) The buyer can take the item at the full stated price or return it
C) The buyer can either take at full price or deduct and keep
D) The contract becomes void automatically

Key Takeaway
Dishonesty in a trust-based sale does not void the contract; the remedy depends on the contract type and the imam's view, with Abu Hanifa's position being the relied-upon one.

Rulings on Murabaha Statements and Inclusion of Expenses
Rules on seller's statement and expense inclusion in murabaha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the seller's statement in murabaha and identify which expenses are included based on custom.

Core Idea
In murabaha, the seller must be truthful; expenses are included only if custom attaches them to the cost.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the key rules for murabaha and tawliya sales. The author emphasizes the importance of honesty in stating the cost and clarifies that extra expenses like teaching a slave are not automatically included. Instead, Hanafi fiqh relies on custom ('urf) to determine which costs become part of the capital.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on the seller's statement
Note that the seller must say 'it cost me such' rather than 'I bought it' to avoid lying. Lying is haram.
This applies to inherited items and goods with written prices.
2
Recognize the principle for including expenses
Expenses are only included if there is an established custom ('urf) that they become part of the capital. Without custom, they are not included.
The passage lists examples: herder wages, teaching fees, storage rent, doctor fees, etc., are not included unless customary.
3
Understand the reasoning (talil) for teaching expenses
Teaching a slave does not increase the capital because the increase in value comes from the slave's own aptitude, not the money spent. This is analogous to dyeing fabric where the fabric's readiness is a condition.
The analogy highlights that the expense is not the direct cause of value increase.
4
Apply the custom test to other expenses
For any expense, ask: Does the local custom consider this as part of the cost? If yes, include; otherwise do not.
The passage mentions that even unjust exactions are included if custom so dictates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المرابحة والتولية ۱۸۳ بكذا ولا يضم أجرة الراعي والتعليم وكراء بيت الحفظ فإن خان في مرابحة أخذ بكل ثمنه أو رده وحط في التولية قوله : (ويقول قام علي بكذا) ولا يقول اشتريته لأنه كذب وهو حرام ولذا قدمنا أنه إذا قوم الموروث ونحوه يقول ذلك وكذا إذا رقم على الثوب شيئاً وباعه برقمه فإنه يقول رقمه كذا وسواء كان ما رقمه موافقاً لما اشتراه به أو أزيد حيث كان صادقاً في الرقم كما في فتح القدير قوله: (ولا يضم أجرة الراعي والتعليم وكراء بيت الحفظ) لعدم العرف بإلحاقه. أطلق في التعليم فشمل تعليم العبد صناعة أو قرآناً أو علماً أو شعراً أو غناء أو عربية قالوا : لأن ثبوت الزيادة لمعنى في العبد وهو حذاقته فلم يكن ما أنفقه على المعلم موجباً للزيادة في المالية، ولا يخفى ما فيه إذ لا شك في حصول الزيادة بالتعلم ولا شك أنه مسبب عن التعليم عادة وكونه بمساعدة القابلية في المتعلم هو كقابلية الثوب للصبغ نسبته إلى التعليم فهو شرط علة عادية والقابلية شرط وفي المبسوط : أضاف نفي ضم المنفق في التعليم إلى أنه ليس فيه عرف ظاهر حتى لو كان فيه عرف ظاهر يلحق برأس المال؛ في فتح القدير. وأشار المؤلف إلى أنه لا يضم أجرة الطبيب والرائض والبيطار والداء في الجناية وجعل الآبق لندرته فلا يلحق بالسابق لأنه لا عرف في النادر والحجامة والختان لعدم العرف، وكذا لا يضم نفقة نفسه وكراءه ولا مهر العبد ولا يحط مهر الأمة لزوجها، والذي يؤخذ في الطريق من الظلم لا يضم إلا في موضع جرت العادة فيه بينهم بالضم . يمنع كذا فلا
Book of sale, chapter of murabaha and tawliya: 183. ...and he does not include the wage of the herder, teaching, and rent of the storage house. If he cheats in murabaha, he takes the entire price or returns it and deducts in tawliya. He said: (And he says: it cost me such) and he does not say: I bought it, because it is a lie and it is unlawful. And thus we have previously stated that when he values an inherited item and the like, he says that. Likewise if he wrote a price on a garment and sold it at that written price, he says: its written price is such, whether the written price agrees with what he bought it for or more, as long as he is truthful in the written price, as in Fath al-Qadir. He said: (And he does not include the wage of the herder, teaching, and rent of the storage house) due to lack of custom to attach it. He made it absolute in teaching, so it includes teaching the slave a craft, Quran, knowledge, poetry, singing, or Arabic. They said: because the increase is due to a quality in the slave, namely his skill, so what he spent on the teacher does not cause an increase in value. But it is not hidden what is in this, for there is no doubt that increase occurs through learning, and there is no doubt that it is normally caused by teaching, and it being assisted by the learner's aptitude is like the fabric's aptitude for dyeing, its relation to teaching is a customary cause, and the aptitude is a condition. And in al-Mabsut: he added the negation of including the expenditure on teaching to the fact that there is no apparent custom, so if there were an apparent custom it would be attached to the capital; in Fath al-Qadir. And the author indicated that he does not include the wage of the doctor, the trainer, the veterinarian, the compensation for injury, and making the runaway slave [not included] due to its rarity, so it is not attached to the preceding, because there is no custom in what is rare, and cupping and circumcision due to lack of custom. Likewise, he does not include his own maintenance and rent, nor the slave's dowry, nor does he deduct the slave-girl's dowry for her husband, and what is taken on the road by injustice is not included except in a place where custom among them is to include it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the rules of murabaha and tawliya in Hanafi fiqh. The author first addresses the seller's statement: he should say 'it cost me such' rather than 'I bought it for such' because the latter could be a lie if the price changed, and lying is haram. This applies when selling inherited goods or goods with a written price. Then the commentator discusses which expenses can be included in the capital cost for calculating profit. The general principle is that only expenses that custom attaches to the price are included. Teaching a slave, for example, is not included because the increase in value is due to the slave's acquired skill, not the money spent on teaching. The same applies to wages of a herder, storage, doctor, trainer, etc. However, if local custom includes such expenses, they may be included. The commentator explains the reasoning (talil) that custom ('urf) is the determinant, and rare cases (nawadir) are not considered.

Key Terms
مرابحة (murabaha): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a specified profit margin.
تولية (tawliya): A sale at exactly the original cost without profit, transferring ownership at the purchase price.
عرف (urf): Customary practice that determines whether an expense is included in the capital cost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi murabaha, if a seller teaches a slave a skill, can he include the teaching fee in the capital cost?
A) Yes, because the slave’s value increases.
B) No, because there is no custom to include it and the increase is due to the slave’s aptitude.
C) Yes, if the seller is truthful.
D) No, but only if the teaching was to learn the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) is the decisive factor for including expenses in murabaha; the seller must be truthful and only include what is customary.

Remedy for Fraud in Murabaha and Tawliya
Intra-Hanafi dispute on remedy for fraud in murabaha and tawliya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding the remedy for fraud in murabaha and tawliya, and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
In tawliya, deduction is forced; in murabaha, option is allowed—Abu Hanifa's distinction between profit and non-profit sales.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens when a seller commits fraud (khianah) by misrepresenting the original cost in a murabaha or tawliya sale. The three great imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—differ on the appropriate remedy. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi school's approach to contractual remedies and the reasoning behind the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the remedy each imam gives for murabaha and tawliya: Abu Hanifa (deduction tawliya, option murabaha), Abu Yusuf (deduction in both), Muhammad (option in both).
2
Examine Muhammad's reasoning
He considers the designation (tawliya/murabaha) a desirable attribute, so loss gives option.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's reasoning
He emphasizes building on the first price, so deduction is necessary in both.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's reasoning
He distinguishes: tawliya requires exact cost so deduction is forced; murabaha allows profit variation so option is feasible.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's position. Also consider how fraud is proven (confession, evidence, oath refusal).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن خان في مرابحة أخذ بكل ثمنه أو رده وحط في التولية) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف يحط فيهما . وقال محمد يخير فيهما . لمحمد أن الاعتبار للتسمية لكونه معلوماً والتولية والمرابحة ترويج وترغيب فتكون وصفاً مرغوباً فيه كوصف السلامة فيتخير لفواته. ولأبي يوسف أن الأصل فيه كونه تولية ومرابحة ولهذا ينعقد بقوله وليتك بالثمن الأول أو بعتك مرابحة على الثمن الأول إذا كان معلوماً فلا بد من البناء على الأول وذلك بالحط غير أنه يحط في التولية قدر الخيانة من رأس المال، وفي المرابحة منه ومن الربح. ولأبي حنيفة أنه لو لم يحط في التولية لا تبقى تولية لأنه يزيد على الثمن الأول فتغير التصرف فتعين الحط، وفي المرابحة لو لم يحط تبقى مرابحة وإن كان يتفاوت الربح فلا يتغير التصرف فأمكن القول بالتخيير . ولم يذكر المصنف والشارح بما تظهر الخيانة قال في فتح القدير : هي إما بإقرار البائع أو بالبينة أو بنكوله عن اليمين وقد ادعاه المشتري هذا على المختار، وقيل لا تثبت إلا بإقراره لأنه في دعوى الخيانة مناقض فلا يتصور ببينة ولا نكول والحق سماعها كدعوى العيب وكدعوى الحط فإنها تسمع اهـ. وقوله «وحط» أي أسقط قدر المسمى. وفي السراج الوهاج وصورة الخيانة في التولية إذا اشترى ثوباً بتسعة وقبضه ثم قال لآخر اشتريته بعشرة ووليتك بما اشتريته فاطلع على ذلك. وبيان الحط في المرابحة على قول أبي يوسف إذا اشتراه بعشرة وباعه بربح خمسة ثم ظهر أنه اشتراه بثمانية فإنه يحط قدر الخيانة من الأصل وهو الخمس وهو درهمان وما قابله من الربح وهو درهم فيأخذ الثوب بإثني عشر درهماً .اهـ. وقدمنا أنه إذا اشترى متاعاً ورقمه بأكثر من ثمنه وباعه مرابحة على الرقم فإنه يجوز . وقيده في المحيط بما إذا كان عند البائع أن المشتري يعلم أن الرقم غير الثمن فأما إذا كان المشتري يعلم أن الرقم والثمن سواء فإنه يكون خيانة وله الخيار؛ كذا في المحيط. وأشار الحط بعدم في التولية إلى أن المشتري إذا وجد بالمبيع عيباً ثم حدث به عيب بنقصان العيب لأنه لو رجع يصير الثمن الثاني أنقص من الأول، وقضية التولية أن يكون مثل الأول وهذا مستثنى من قولهم في خيار العيب، وبقوله رده إلى اشتراط قيام المبيع بحاله فلو هلك قبل رده أو حدث به ما يمنع الرد لزمه بجميع المسمى وسقط خياره عند أبي حنيفة وهو المشهور من قول محمد لأنه مجرد خيار فلا يقابله شيء من الثمن كخيار الرؤية والشرط بخلاف خيار العيب لأن المستحق فيه للمشتري الجزء الفائت. وظاهر كلامهم أن خيار ظهور الخيانة لا يورث فإذا مات المشتري فأطلع الوارث على خيانة بالطريق السابق فلا خيار له وأطلق الحط في التولية فشمل حالة هلاك المبيع وامتناع رده لأنه لا خيار له وإنما يلزمه الثمن الأول. وفي المحيط وإن ضم إلى الثمن ما لا يجوز ضمه ثم علم به المشتري فله الخيار اهـ.
He said: (If he cheats in murabaha, he takes the entire price or returns it, and deducts in tawliya) and this is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: he deducts in both. Muhammad said: he gives option in both. For Muhammad, the consideration is the designation because it is known, and tawliya and murabaha are promotion and persuasion, so they become a desirable description like the description of safety, so he has option due to its loss. For Abu Yusuf, the basis is that it is tawliya and murabaha, and for this reason it is concluded by his saying 'I assign you at the first price' or 'I sell you as murabaha on the first price' if it is known, so building on the first is necessary, and that is by deducting, except that he deducts in tawliya the amount of the fraud from the capital, and in murabaha from it and from the profit. For Abu Hanifa, if he did not deduct in tawliya it would not remain tawliya because he exceeds the first price, so the transaction changes, so deduction is determined; in murabaha if he did not deduct it remains murabaha, although the profit differs, so the transaction does not change, so the possibility of option is allowed. The author and commentator did not mention by what the fraud appears. Al-Fath al-Qadir said: it is either by the seller's confession, or by evidence, or by his refusal to take an oath when the buyer claims it, according to the chosen view. It was said: it is only established by his confession, because he is inconsistent in the claim of fraud, so it cannot be imagined by evidence or refusal; but the correct view is that it is heard like a claim of defect or a claim of deduction, for they are heard. And his saying 'and deducts' means he drops the amount named. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the form of fraud in tawliya is: if he bought a garment for nine and took possession, then said to another 'I bought it for ten and I assign you at what I bought it for' and he discovers that. The explanation of deduction in murabaha according to Abu Yusuf: if he bought it for ten and sold it at a profit of five, then it appears he bought it for eight, then he deducts the amount of fraud from the capital, which is two dirhams, and its corresponding from the profit, which is one dirham, so he takes the garment for twelve dirhams. We have already stated that if he bought goods and wrote a price higher than its cost and sold it as murabaha on that written price, it is permissible. Al-Muhit restricted it to when the seller knows that the buyer knows the written price is not the cost; but if the buyer knows the written price and the cost are equal, then it is fraud and he has option. In al-Muhit, if he includes in the price what should not be included, then the buyer knows it, he has option. The indication of not deducting in tawliya is that if the buyer finds a defect in the sold item then a new defect occurs, due to the decrease from the defect, because if he returns it the second price becomes less than the first, and the requirement of tawliya is that it be like the first. This is an exception from their statement about the option of defect. And by his saying 'or returns it' it requires the sold item to remain in its state, so if it perishes before return or something occurs that prevents return, he is liable for the entire named price and his option falls, according to Abu Hanifa, and this is the well-known view of Muhammad, because it is a mere option so nothing of the price corresponds to it, like the option of sight and condition, unlike the option of defect because what is due to the buyer is the lost part. And it is apparent from their statements that the option for fraud is not inherited, so if the buyer dies and the heir discovers fraud in the previous manner, he has no option. And he made deduction absolute in tawliya, so it includes the case of destruction of the sold item and prevention of return, because he has no option but is liable for the first price. In al-Muhit, if he includes in the price what should not be included, then the buyer knows it, he has option.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the remedy when fraud (khianah) is discovered in a murabaha or tawliya sale. The text is commentary on the matn 'If he cheats in murabaha, he takes the entire price or returns it, and deducts in tawliya.' Abu Hanifa holds that in tawliya, the seller must deduct the fraudulent amount, but in murabaha, the buyer has the option either to take at the higher price or return. Abu Yusuf argues that in both contracts, the seller must deduct the fraudulent amount from the agreed price (in murabaha, from both capital and profit). Muhammad holds that in both, the buyer has the option. Each imam provides reasoning: Muhammad sees the designation as a desirable attribute, so its loss gives option. Abu Yusuf emphasizes building on the original price, which requires deduction. Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in tawliya, no option is possible because the price must match the original cost; in murabaha, profit can vary, so option is feasible. The commentator then discusses how fraud is proven: by confession, evidence, or refusal to take oath. The relied-upon view is that all these are valid. The text also explains the calculation of deduction with an example and covers related issues like written price, defect, and inheritance of the option.

Key Terms
خيانة (khianah): Fraud where the seller misrepresents the original cost in a murabaha or tawliya sale.
حط (hatt): Deduction from the price equal to the amount of fraud (from capital and/or profit).
خيار (khiyar): The buyer's option to either uphold the contract at the original price or rescind it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the remedy for fraud in a murabaha contract?
A) The buyer must deduct the fraudulent amount from the price.
B) The buyer has the option to take the item at the original price or return it.
C) The seller must deduct the fraud from both capital and profit.
D) The contract is automatically void.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the remedy for fraud differs by contract type: tawliya requires deduction, murabaha grants an option—a distinction rooted in the nature of profit.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Murabaha After Repurchase: Deducting Previous Profit
Intra-Hanafi dispute on murabaha after repurchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on murabaha after repurchase and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between them.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: previous profit must be deducted from the new cost base; Sahibayn: the new purchase is independent.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about a recurring commercial scenario: a merchant buys a garment, sells it at a profit, then buys the same garment again, and wishes to resell it on a murabaha basis (cost-plus). The core question is whether the second purchase is a fresh start or whether past profits affect the cost base. Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) offer different answers, and the practical implications are significant for merchants.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling scenario
Identify the sequence: buy → sell at profit → rebuy → sell again on murabaha. Note the two examples given in the text.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa requires deducting all previous profit from the new purchase price when calculating the cost basis for the second murabaha sale. If the previous profit equals or exceeds the new purchase price, no murabaha is allowed at all.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
The two companions hold that the second purchase is a completely new and independent contract. Therefore, the murabaha can be based on the last purchase price without deducting past profit, as if a third party had intervened.
4
Analyze each side's dalil (proof)
Abu Hanifa argues from a 'shubhah' - the suspicion that the seller is effectively selling to himself and the profit is unrealized. The Sahibayn argue from the independence of the new contract, comparing it to a transfer to a third party.
The text notes 'shubhah' for Abu Hanifa and 'aqd mutajaddid' for the Sahibayn.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In practice, Abu Hanifa's ruling leads to a lower cost basis (original cost minus past profit), possibly preventing murabaha if no profit remains. The Sahibayn allow murabaha on the full new purchase price, yielding a higher potential profit.
Example from text: buy 10, sell 15, rebuy 10 → Abu Hanifa basis = 5; Sahibayn basis = 10.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن اشترى ثوباً فباعه بربح ثم اشتراه فإن باعه بربح طرح عنه كل ربح قبله وإن أحاط بثمنه لم يرابح وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا يبيعه مرابحة على الثمن الأخير وصورته إذا اشترى ثوباً بعشرة وباعه بخمسة عشر ثم اشتراه بعشرة فإنه يبيعه مرابحة بخمسة ويقول قام علي بخسمة، ولو اشتراه بعشرة وباعه بعشرين مرابحة ثم اشتراه بعشرة لا مرابحة أصلاً. وعندهما يرابح على عشرة في الفصلين لهما أن العقد الثاني عقد متجدد منقطع الأحكام عن الأول فيجوز بناء المرابحة عليه كما إذا تخلل ثالث . ولأبي حنيفة أن شبهة يبيعه فليتأمل. قوله : (وأشار بعدم الحط في التولية كذا في بعض النسخ وفي بعضها وأشار بالحط» وهو
He said: (And whoever buys a garment and sells it at a profit, then buys it again, if he sells it at a profit he deducts all previous profit; if he encompasses its price he does not do murabaha) and this is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) said: he sells it as murabaha on the last price. Its form: if he buys a garment for ten and sells it for fifteen, then buys it for ten, he sells it as murabaha for five and says: it cost me five. If he buys it for ten and sells it for twenty as murabaha, then buys it for ten, there is no murabaha at all. According to them, he does murabaha on ten in both cases, because the second contract is a new contract independent of the first, so building murabaha on it is permissible, as if a third person intervened. According to Abu Hanifa, due to the suspicion that he sells it... so let it be pondered. He said: (And he indicated by not deducting in tawliya) thus in some copies, and in some copies 'by deducting' and it is...
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute about a scenario where a person buys a garment, sells it at a profit, then buys the same garment again, and then wishes to sell it again on murabaha. Abu Hanifa rules that when the second sale is at a profit, the seller must deduct all previous profit from the cost; if the second purchase price equals or exceeds the previous profit, no murabaha is allowed. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the second purchase is a new contract, so the murabaha can be based on the last purchase price. They illustrate: buying for 10, selling for 15, then buying for 10 again – the seller can do murabaha on 10 saying 'it cost me 5' (since he already made 5 profit). If he bought for 10, sold for 20, then bought for 10, no murabaha according to Abu Hanifa because the previous profit (10) equals the new price; but the Sahibayn allow murabaha on 10. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is based on the 'suspicion' (shubhah) that the profit from the first sale might be considered as reducing the effective cost. The text ends abruptly with a note on variant readings about deduction in tawliya.

Key Terms
طرح الربح (tarh al-ribh): Deducting all previous profit from the cost base when reselling in murabaha after repurchase.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt or semblance of right that prevents certain transactions, here the suspicion that the profit is effectively returned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone buys a garment for 10, sells it for 15 (murabaha), then buys it back for 10, what is the cost basis for the next murabaha sale?
A) 10 (the new purchase price)
B) 5 (after deducting the previous profit of 5)
C) 15 (the previous sale price)
D) No murabaha is possible because the profit is 0.

Key Takeaway
When reselling a repurchased item on murabaha, Abu Hanifa deducts past profit while the Sahibayn treat the repurchase as a fresh start.
